# Phase K — in-game opcode handlers + UDP proxy plane

Goal: take the Phase J "TLS terminates, handshake works, opcodes are dispatched" baseline and turn it into actually playable login → enter sector → see other players. Each item is sized to be portable independently (file-level WIN32 walls drop one at a time).

## Carry-over from Phase J

- TCP 3500 (SECTOR_SERVER_PORT) has no listener on Linux. `HandleMasterJoin` sends a hardcoded ServerRedirect there.
- `ProcessGlobalServerOpcode` (`proxy/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp`, 286 LOC, ~15 handlers) is a Linux logging stub.
- `ProcessSectorServerOpcode` (`proxy/ClientToSectorServer.cpp`, 757 LOC, ~50+ handlers) is a Linux logging stub.
- UDP proxy plane (`proxy/UDPProxyMVAS.cpp`, `UDPProxyToClient.cpp`, `UDPProxyToGlobal.cpp`, `UDPClient.cpp`) compiles to nothing on Linux.
- Login ticket handoff (login → game server) not wired. Win32 path is `RegisterSectorServer` over SSL on SSL_LOCALCERT_LOGIN_PORT (3807); endpoint not bound on Linux.
- `net7ssl` has no per-connection threading — single-request / single-response per TLS session. Fine for dev; not fine for load.
- `/who.cgi` is a 404 stub (depends on PlayerManager).

## Items

- [x] Bind TCP 3500 (SECTOR_SERVER_PORT) accept loop in the Linux proxy and publish it on the host docker-compose port map.
      Status: done — bind was already there (proxy/ServerManager.cpp:76 unconditional `TcpListener sector_comms(..., SECTOR_SERVER_PORT, ..., CLIENT_TO_SECTOR_SERVER)`); accepted sockets already route through the same Connection ctor / RC4 handshake / framed dispatch as 3801. Only missing piece was the host port publish.
      Touches: `docker-compose.yml` (added `"3500:3500/tcp"` under proxy.ports).
      Notes: Verified end-to-end: `exec 3<>/dev/tcp/127.0.0.1/3500` succeeds from the host, proxy logs `accept on port 3500 from 172.18.0.1` + `DoKeyExchange: ...` (handshake starts then fails on empty input — expected for a no-op test connection). Integration suite still 5/5.

- [x] Port `ProcessMasterServerOpcode` chain end-to-end (avatar select → ServerRedirect). Currently `HandleMasterJoin` is the only handler exercised; full table at `proxy/ClientToMasterServer.cpp:Process…`.
      Status: done — ProcessMasterServerOpcode in `proxy/ClientToMasterServer.cpp:30-43` only dispatches one opcode (0x0035 MASTER_JOIN); everything else falls into the UNRECOGNIZED OPCODE default and logs. Linux HandleMasterJoin (Phase J commit 5bd0afd / 6ffe642) drives the full SendMasterLogin → ServerRedirect flow via the UDP plane subset (commit a357d11), with a Phase J fallback to hardcoded local ServerRedirect on UDP timeout. The "chain end-to-end" framing was based on a wrong assumption that the master server had multiple handlers — the design is much simpler: master server = one opcode in, one opcode out. The deeper avatar-select flow lives in ProcessGlobalServerOpcode, not here.
      Notes: live `MasterJoin.LiveMasterJoinReturnsServerRedirect` test covers this end-to-end (6/7 in `just integration-test`). The UDP plane fallback path is exercised because server-side HandleMasterHandoff is still a stub (carries forward as a server-side Phase K item, separate from the proxy port).

- [~] Port `ProcessGlobalServerOpcode` handlers. Group by dependency on UDP plane vs. pure-TCP — port pure-TCP ones first.
      Status: in progress — five handlers ported and verified end-to-end this phase. (a) VersionRequest 0x0000 → VersionResponse 0x0001 (pure-TCP). (b) GlobalConnect 0x006D → GlobalAvatarList 0x0070 (via UDP_GLOBAL_SERVER_PORT 3810; both happy path and STRESS_TEST_CLOSED rejection covered). (c) GlobalTicketRequest 0x006E → GlobalTicket 0x006F (via SendAvatarLogin; failure path tested — galaxy-full timeout returns response_code=1002, exercises UDP_Global.cpp's wire-size fix). (d) GlobalDeleteCharacter 0x0071 → GlobalAvatarList refresh (via SendDeleteCharacter UDP round-trip; landed alongside PacketMethods.h ExtractLong cast bugfix). (e) GlobalCreateCharacter 0x0072 → GlobalAvatarList refresh (via SendCreateCharacter UDP round-trip; landed alongside ColorInfo/ShipData/GlobalCreateCharacter long→int32_t migration AND the GlobalAvatarListCodec AvatarData offset fix AND the sql_query AppendValue UB fix). Only **ProcessGlobalTicket** carries forward — it's the inbound-from-server side that drives 0x006F handoff post-AvatarLogin; the integration test today exercises only the failure branch where the timeout never produces a ticket. The Linux dispatcher lives in `proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp`; unimplemented opcodes still log + return for visibility into what real clients send.
      Touches done: `proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp` (Linux ProcessGlobalServerOpcode dispatch — VersionRequest, GlobalConnect, GlobalTicketRequest, GlobalDeleteCharacter, GlobalCreateCharacter, GlobalError forwarding, GlobalAvatarList forwarding), `tests/client/version_request_test.cpp` (live test), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/{GlobalConnect,GlobalTicketRequest,GlobalDeleteCharacter,GlobalCreateCharacter}Tests.cs` (round-trip coverage), `server/src/PacketMethods.h` (ExtractLong cast `long*` → `int32_t*`), `server/src/mysql/mysqlplus.cpp` (sql_query AppendValue helper — see decisions log 2026-05-24), `common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h` (ColorInfo/ShipData/GlobalCreateCharacter long→int32_t), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/Inbound/GlobalAvatarListCodec.cs` (AvatarData offsets race=46/prof=50/gender=54/mood=58 — ATTRIB_PACKED has no implicit padding).

      Notes: cli-integration 38/38 green from a fresh `docker compose down -v`. Coverage floor: TestedOpcodes.cs MinTestedCount 7→11 (added 0x006E/0x006F/0x0071/0x0072).

(g) TURN 0x0012 rate-limited 1 per 250ms via m_Turn_Sent. (h) TILT 0x0013 same cadence with m_Tilt_Sent. (i) ACTION 0x002C explicit forward + ProcessAction_Linux helper (all 6 Win32 sub-cases are //commented-out logs, no-op). KillTCPConnection from Win32's PLAYER_SHIP_SENT branch lives in WIN32-walled UDPProxyToClient.cpp — skipped; equivalent close happens naturally as server tears state. Default case also forwards (Win32 line 108): server is authority on opcode-meaningful-in-state, proxy just relays.

- [~] Port the UDP proxy plane (`UDPClient`, `UDPProxyMVAS`, `UDPProxyToClient`, `UDPProxyToGlobal`). POSIX UDP sockets + blocking recv thread.
      Status: minimum-viable subset done — HandleMasterJoin now drives a real SendMasterLogin -> server:3808 UDP exchange.
      Touches: `proxy/UDPClient_linux.cpp` (new, ~390 LOC; POSIX socket + bind to INADDR_ANY:0 ephemeral + connect to game-server:3808, pthread-launched blocking recv thread, full subset for SendMasterLogin + MasterLoginConfirm + WaitForResponse + FixedClientComm; getenv("NET7_GAME_SERVER_HOST") default "server" via getaddrinfo, no hardcoded IP), `proxy/ClientToMasterServer.cpp` (Linux HandleMasterJoin now mirrors the Win32 path: SendMasterLogin -> set port/ip/sector -> SendServerRedirect; falls back to the Phase J option-b local ServerRedirect on -1 timeout), `proxy/Net7.cpp` (Linux main constructs `UDPClient(MVAS_LOGIN_PORT, FIXED, ip_internal)` and registers it as BOTH m_UDPConnection and m_UDPClient — Win32 used two distinct FIXED+MULTI instances; on Linux we only port FIXED so one object serves both roles).
      Notes: docker logs show "UDPClient: resolved game server 'server' -> 172.18.0.6 / UDPClient: bound UDP <ephem> (src) -> 172.18.0.6:3808". Live integration test `MasterJoin.LiveMasterJoinReturnsServerRedirect` goes green; `just integration-test` 6/6. SendMasterLogin currently times out after ~5s (server-side HandleMasterHandoff is "Unimplemented opcode" stub — see server/src/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp:488) and falls through to the local ServerRedirect; the proxy wiring is correct end-to-end. Still WIN32-walled on Linux (not on the MasterJoin->ServerRedirect path; portable independently as their opcode handlers land): position-update thread (`UDPProxyMVAS::MVASThread`), avatar/ticket/global-error UDP path (`UDPProxyToGlobal.cpp` minus the SendMasterLogin slice that lives in UDPClient_linux.cpp), keep-alive / packet-sequence resend, OpenMultiPort / CLIENT_TYPE_MULTI_PORT (client-only).

- [x] Wave 6 (2026-05-24): server→client UDP fan-out (`UDPProxyToClient.cpp` Linux port).
      Status: done — `proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp` (new, ~370 LOC) implements the master-plane recv side that was missing from Wave 3: `ProcessClientOpcode` (direct passthrough to `m_SectorConnection->SendResponse`), `IncommingOpcodePreProcessing` (LOGOFF / SERVER_HANDOFF / START state transitions), `SendClientDataFile` (0x2010 — forward verbatim except 0x0097 galaxy map which is logged), `SendPacketSequence` + `SendLoginPacketSequence` (full reliable-delivery + split-packet reassembly, mirrors Win32 UDPProxyToClient.cpp:138-351 line-for-line with usleep/check_memory swaps), `SendClientPacketSequence` (walks inner [size,opcode,data] tuples; dispatches one TCP frame per opcode via SendResponse since the WIN32-only Queue*/SendQueuedPacket batchers don't exist on Linux), `HandleCustomOpcode` (minimal — 0x2020 stage confirm + 0x100A terminate; launcher-side opcodes 0x2011-0x2019 return false to let the outer raw-forward path fire), `HandleStageConfirm` (sends 0x2021 ACK back to server), `SendCommsAlive`, `RecordLastHandoff`, `KillTCPConnection` no-op. RecvThread switch in `proxy/UDPClient_linux.cpp` extended with the four new dispatches (0x2010 / 0x2016 / 0x201A / default → ProcessClientOpcode). `proxy/Connection.cpp` Linux SendResponse now takes `m_Mutex` around m_CryptOut + m_SendBuffer + SendAll because the UDP RecvThread is now a concurrent producer with the TCP RecvThread. File-scope `bool g_ShuttingDown = false;` and `uint32_t time_debug = 0;` defined in the new file (Win32 origins are WIN32-walled). What this does NOT include: SendDataFileToClient cache path (depends on WIN32-walled ClientToSectorServer.cpp::SendDataFile) — galaxy-map cache request is logged-no-op; launcher Queue* helpers — opcodes 0x2011/0x2012/0x2013/0x2014/0x2018/0x2019 are forwarded raw rather than batched.
      Touches: `proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp` (new file), `proxy/UDPClient_linux.cpp` (RecvThread switch + file-comment update), `proxy/Connection.cpp` (Mutex around Linux SendResponse + comment update).
      Notes: clean build, cli-integration 38/38 green from existing stack. Wave 6 unblocks Task #69 (sector LOGIN 0x0002 → START round-trip) — server can now reply to a sector-port client and the proxy will deliver the reply over TCP.

- [!] Wire ticket handoff: bind SSL_LOCALCERT_LOGIN_PORT (3807) on the game server, validate ticket against the same store that net7ssl issued from. Decide: shared MySQL `tickets` table vs. AF_UNIX SOCK_DGRAM push from login to server.
      Status: blocked / re-scoped after Win32 design discovery — there's no cross-process ticket state to share. The Win32 `AccountManager::GetUsernameFromTicket` (login-server/Net7SSL/AccountManager.cpp:839) and the server-side equivalent (`server/src/AccountManager.cpp`) both validate a ticket by `strchr(ticket, '-')` and taking the prefix as the username. The format is `<username>-<rand()>`, with no signature, MAC, or shared secret. "Validation" is effectively a username extraction; anyone who knows a valid username can construct a ticket the server will accept. SSL_LOCALCERT_LOGIN_PORT 3807 is the *other* direction (game server registers itself with login, not ticket transfer) — see Win32 `SSL_Connection.cpp:628 RegisterSectorServer(m_IpAddress, port_number, num_sectors, username)` which adds the sector server to the login service's known-sectors list for ServerRedirect routing decisions.
      Reason for `[!]`: closing as "blocked" because the original framing was wrong; building real ticket sharing now would diverge from Win32 parity. Real cryptographic ticket validation belongs in a future security-hardening Phase, not Phase K. The minimum-viable port already does the right thing — login issues `<user>-<rand>`, proxy/server parses with `strtok(ticket, "-")` and trusts it.
      Touches done (parity): `login-server/Net7SSL/LinuxAuth.cpp:82 BuildTicketLocked` (issues `<user>-<rand>`), `proxy/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp:134` (Win32 path: `strtok(ticket, "-")`).
      Touches remaining (parity): port the `strtok` line into the Linux HandleGlobalConnect when that handler is implemented (carries with `ProcessGlobalServerOpcode` item).
      Open follow-up (out of scope for Phase K): replace string-format ticket with HMAC-signed token, per RFC 6750-style bearer; shared MySQL or Redis ticket store; cap-share between processes via 60-second TTL.

- [x] PacketStructures.h `long` → `int32_t` migration. The structs sent over the wire use `long`, which is 4 bytes on Win32 and 8 bytes on Linux x86_64. This makes MasterJoin 64 vs 108 bytes and ServerRedirect 10 vs 18 bytes. Half the bug also lived in `proxy/Connection.cpp` Linux SendResponse, which stamped `size = payload + sizeof(long)` (= 8) leaving a 4-byte gap between header and payload.
      Status: in progress — wire structs on the Linux dispatch + UDP master plane migrated. (a) Linux SendResponse `sizeof(long)` → `sizeof(EnbTcpHeader)`. (b) `ServerRedirect` 18B→10B (`port` now at offset 8 on every platform). (c) `VersionRequest` 16B→8B — was working by coincidence (test sends 8B payload; Linux struct's 8B `long` fields aliased the wire bytes thanks to LE truncation in `(uint32_t) request->Major` plus zero-padding for `Minor`). (d) `MasterJoin` 108B→64B — this was the real win. Before: HandleMasterJoin read `avatar_id_lsb`/`ToSectorID` from offsets 32/40 (8-byte field layout), saw zeros, hit the `SendMasterLogin timed-out` fallback path. After: log line now reads `avatar_id=1 ToSectorID=1` from the synthesized test, and `avatar_id=4150549696 ToSectorID=45151` from the captured Win32-client replay — actual captured values, finally parsed correctly. (e) `EnbUdpHeader` 20B→12B + ATTRIB_PACKED — `player_id` + `packet_sequence` were both `long`, so every UDP frame between proxy and server carried an 8-byte gap that a real Win32 client never produces. Server and proxy recompile from the same header so the size flip is symmetric on the Linux-only path. Remaining: other wire structs not yet exercised by the Linux dispatch (GlobalAvatarList, ServerHandoff, GlobalCreateCharacter, Login, et al.) and per-handler memcpy targets.
      Touches done: `proxy/Connection.cpp` (Linux SendResponse), `common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h` — **complete migration**, every `long`/`unsigned long` wire-struct field declaration converted to `int32_t`/`uint32_t`; per-struct comments document why; structs covered in order of when they landed: (a) early 2026-05-24 wave: ServerRedirect, VersionRequest, MasterJoin, EnbTcpHeader, EnbUdpHeader; (b) GlobalAvatarList family — AvatarData/AvatarInfo/Galaxy/GlobalAvatarList::num_galaxies — restored 2042B canonical wire size from 2518B Linux x86_64; (c) ColorInfo / ShipData / GlobalCreateCharacter — restored 17B/207B/539B canonical wire sizes from 21B/226B/571B; (d) commit a82459d sweep (this session): WarpPacket, InvMove, InvSort, ItemState, ChangeBaseAsset, Create, ServerParameters, Login, Navigation, CreateAttachment, DecalItem, Decal, NameDecal, ColorizationItem, Colorization, AvatarDescription, Subparts, ConstantPositionalUpdate, FormationPositionalUpdate, RequestTarget, SetInterface, SetTarget, ActionPacket, ActionPacket2, ClientSetTime, VerbRequest, CameraControl, LogoffRequest, TriggerEmote, NotifyEmote, OptionPacket, SelectTalkTree, ChatStream, ClientChat, ClientChatRequest, ClientChatList, ClientChatError, ClientChatEvent, ClientSkillsRequest, StarbaseAvatarChange{,_S2C}, StarbaseRoomChange, StarbaseRequest, Relationship, ObjectEffect, ObjectToObjectEffect, InitRenderState, ActivateRenderState, SimplePositionalUpdate, PlanetPositionalUpdate, ComponentPositionalUpdate, AdvancedPositionalUpdate, EquipUse, AbilityUse, StarbaseSet, ShipInfo, CTARequest, MovePacket, SkillAction, SkillUse, MissionDismissal, MVASHandoff, ManufactureData, ManufactureTechLevelFilter, FindMember (+ nested fm_item), RecustomizeAvatarStart, RecustomizeShipStart, RecustomizeShipDone, RecustomizeAvatarDone. Knock-on fix: `Player::SetupWarpNavs(short, long *)` decl/defn updated to take `int32_t *target_id` to match WarpPacket.TargetID's migrated type. Also: `server/src/UDP_Master.cpp` (related wire bugs: `sector_id` was over-read 8B for a 4B field; termination packet sent `sizeof(long)=8` where wire expects 4); `server/src/UDP_Global.cpp` (HandleGlobalTicketRequest cast fixes; AVATARLOGIN_CONFIRM reply size 8B→4B); `tests/client/master_join_test.cpp` (probe simplified to {8}).
      Notes: post-Phase-R there is only one PacketStructures.h (under common/) — sibling copies under server/src/ and login-server/Net7SSL/ no longer exist. Post-sweep: server + proxy + login-server build clean; `just cli-integration` 38/38 green from a fresh `docker compose down -v` rebuild. The sweep does NOT cover raw byte-buffer `*((long *) &data[N])` reads in `server/src/SaveManager.cpp` and elsewhere — those are the same class of Linux-port bug (8B reads from 4B wire slots) but live outside PacketStructures.h; tracked as a separate follow-up since they're more invasive (each call site needs the slot offset and surrounding reads verified against the wire frame).

- [x] Per-connection threading in net7ssl (Linux) — detached worker thread per accepted SSL session so a slow handshake doesn't head-of-line block other connects.
      Status: done — `SSL_Listener::HandleAcceptedConnection` runs SSL_accept + read + dispatch + write + close on a detached `std::thread`. Capped at 64 concurrent workers (std::atomic counter); over-cap connections are refused with a log line so a flood can't fork-bomb. Lighter than the Win32 `SSL_Connection` model (no connection pool, no persistent thread per client) but matches the request shape — each TLS session is one round trip.
      Touches: `login-server/Net7SSL/SSL_Listener.h` (+13 LOC: atomic counter, HandleAcceptedConnection decl, <atomic> include), `login-server/Net7SSL/SSL_Listener.cpp` (-50/+65 LOC: inline accept body moves into HandleAcceptedConnection, listener launches detached thread).
      Notes: Verified end-to-end — fired 5 concurrent `curl https://.../AuthLogin` and the proxy log shows 5 interleaved "Accepted SSL connection" / "SSL handshake OK" / "HTTP: GET /AuthLogin" lines instead of strict serial ordering. `just integration-test` 6/6 still green.

- [x] Proxy↔server **global UDP control plane** (UDP_GLOBAL_SERVER_PORT 3810) — wire endpoint for the avatar-list handoff that the kyp-era TCP cluster (SSL_LOCALCERT_LOGIN_PORT 3807) used to carry before Phase Q deleted it. Round-trip path: client sends 0x006D GlobalConnect on TCP 3805 → proxy `UDPClient(global).SendTicket` writes `[u32 0x2002 TICKET]` to server:3810 → server `UDP_Connection::HandleGlobalOpcode` (server/src/UDP_Global.cpp:43) routes through `ProcessTicketInfo` → reads account from net7_user (status, ticket username via strtok) → constructs Player → `SendAvatarList` writes `[u32 0x2003 AVATARLIST]` back to proxy:UDP → proxy forwards as 0x0070 GLOBAL_AVATAR_LIST on TCP 3805.
      Status: done — cli-integration covers both branches of the plane: `GlobalConnectTests.ValidTicket_RoundTripsThroughUdpGlobalPlane_ReturnsAvatarList` (happy path → 0x0070 GlobalAvatarList) AND `GlobalConnectTests.StressTestClosedAccount_GlobalConnect_ReturnsGlobalErrorCode12` (error path → 0x0075 GlobalError code 12 STRESS_TEST_CLOSED). The error path uses an out-of-pool seed account `cli_test_status0` (id 9000010, status=0) so the happy-path Pool stays clean. 35/35 cli-integration green.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/GlobalConnectTests.cs` (sends 0x006D with `[u32 ticket_len_be][char ticket[len]][NUL]` payload; happy-path test waits for 0x0070 and fails loud with the G_ERROR code if 0x0075 arrives instead; error-path test does the inverse — waits for 0x0075, fails loud if 0x0070 arrives since that would mean someone weakened the server's status check), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (+3 entries for 0x006D + 0x0070 + 0x0075, `MinTestedCount` 4→7), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (`StressTestClosed` accessor out-of-Pool), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Smoke/HarnessSmokeTest.cs` (also asserts seed.sql carries the out-of-pool fixture), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (6th account `cli_test_status0`).
      Notes — diagnostics that lit up while landing this:
       - **Seed-account `status` was the blocker.** Server `ProcessTicketInfo` (UDP_Global.cpp:138-143) hard-rejects `status==0` with `G_ERROR_STRESS_TEST_CLOSED` (12). Pool was seeded with status=0 (boilerplate default from the pre-Phase-K era when login was the only path exercised). Real accounts use status=100 (cf. `net7_user.sql` admin row). Fixed in `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` — status now 100 for all five `cli_test0N` accounts plus an enum-table comment.
       - **Proxy's `g_GlobalErrorMsg[]` was truncated.** Table only had codes 0-11; AccountManager.h defines through code 14. When the server returned code 12 the proxy's `Connection::GlobalError` (proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp) logged "unknown error code 12 — dropping" and the client never saw the rejection, masking the seed bug behind a generic timeout. Fixed: full 0-14 table with comments tying each entry to its `G_ERROR_*` constant.
       - **GlobalAvatarList codec landed (third commit, this session).** PacketStructures.h's AvatarData/AvatarInfo/Galaxy/GlobalAvatarList migrated from `long` to `int32_t` to restore Win32 wire-format parity (mirrors the e74f07c MasterJoin migration). Server rebuilt: GlobalAvatarList now serialises to the canonical 2042 bytes (was 2518 on Linux x86_64 with 8-byte longs — silently divergent from Win32). New `GlobalAvatarListCodec` (tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/Inbound/) decodes the full struct: 5 AvatarSlot pairs (AvatarInfo + AvatarData), num_galaxies, and up to 2 Galaxy entries with name/ip/port/player-counts. Happy-path test now asserts `WireSize == 2042`, all 5 slots zero-filled (seeded `avatars` table is empty), galaxy[0].name non-empty, GalaxyID=1, MaxPlayers>0 — these are stronger evidence than "non-empty payload" that the migration took.
       - **The escape-hatch test (`[!]` blocking) is now gone.** The cli-integration Phase T plan can re-open Items 10-12 (enumerate sectors/missions/items workflows) once a GlobalAvatarList codec lands and an avatar can actually be selected → enter sector.
       - **Error-path coverage added (second commit).** `StressTestClosedAccount_GlobalConnect_ReturnsGlobalErrorCode12` validates the inverse path: client → proxy → server (rejects status=0 in `ProcessTicketInfo`) → proxy (forwards via `Connection::GlobalError` + `g_GlobalErrorMsg[12]`) → client. Test asserts both the error code (12) and the human-readable message text from the proxy's table comes through — proves the proxy-table truncation fix landed correctly and would regress loudly if anyone trimmed `g_GlobalErrorMsg[]` back to 12 entries. It also acts as a server-integrity tripwire: if the status-check weakens, the test fails with a CLAUDE.md citation in the failure message.
      Subsystem unblocked: cli-integration now has both the happy-path and the explicit-rejection round-trip locked in. Adding the next UDP-plane scenario (CreateCharacter / DeleteCharacter / SendAvatarLogin) becomes incremental, not architectural.

- [!] `/who.cgi` HTML output — there is nothing meaningful to port here. Win32 reference (`login-server/Net7SSL/SSL_Connection.cpp:256-260`) is a `//TODO` empty branch that leaves `response = nullptr` and falls through. Server-side `m_PlayerMgr.WhoHtml(response_length)` (`server/src/SSL_Connection.cpp:314`) is **referenced but never defined** — there is no `WhoHtml` symbol anywhere in `server/src/`. The Win32 build links because that branch sits inside `#ifdef WIN32` walls that are never compiled (or it's a runtime fault — neither has been verified). Either way, there's no upstream HTML generator to mirror.
      Status: blocked — moved from `[ ]` to `[!]`. The Linux behavior (`MakeNotFound` 404 in `LinuxAuth.cpp:524-526`) is actually *more honest* than the Win32 fall-through, which silently writes nothing and lets the connection die. Building a real implementation belongs in a future phase that also implements `PlayerManager::WhoHtml` from scratch on both platforms — out of scope for "match Phase K parity."
      Touches if revisited: `login-server/Net7SSL/LinuxAuth.cpp` (HTML response writer), `server/src/PlayerManager.cpp` (new WhoHtml method that lists active players), and an IPC channel (shared file / AF_UNIX socket / DB query) since net7ssl can't reach server PlayerManager directly today.

      Status: done — `server/src/SectorManager.cpp` constructor now initializes `m_JobListCount = 0`. - [x] Wave 7 (cont.) — sector LOGIN 0x0002 → START round-trip wiring (2026-05-25, commits d8bfa44 + 7e15637 + 82d955f + ea6d695 + 3ecc04a).
      Status: done — `SectorLoginTests.FullSectorLogin_ReceivesStart` passes in 7s; full 39-test integration suite passes in 2m33s. Approach diverged from the original "third UDPClient on MVAS plane" sketch: instead of standing up a third connect()'d socket, the **global plane was switched to unconnected** (sendto + recvfrom + IP whitelist), because the server-side reality is that **post-login in-game UDP comes from MVASauth (server:3806) to the proxy's global-plane source port** — not a separate destination. The server captures `player->m_Player_Port` from the AVATARLOGIN packet's source port (server/src/UDP_Global.cpp:227) and from then on all `player->m_UDPConnection` writes go to (proxy_ip, that_port) via MVASauth's socket. A connected SOCK_DGRAM on the global plane filtered by single peer port (3810) and silently dropped MVASauth's 3806 frames. Unconnected mode keeps the default-peer for outgoing sendto() (still routes to 3810 for global-control opcodes 0x2003/0x2005/0x200C/0x200E) while accepting recv() from any source port + dropping non-server source IPs.
      Three classes of bug fixed: (a) **proxy SendPacketSequence calling convention** — Linux UDPClient was passing `msg` (payload-only) where Win32 passes the whole UDP packet; SendClientPacketSequence re-casts buffer to EnbUdpHeader and skipped 12 payload bytes, producing the "bad opcode 0x0000 len 0x0" symptom on every 0x2016 frame. Fix: pass `(char *) m_RecvBuffer` for both 0x2016 and 0x201A. (b) **proxy global plane unconnected** — `proxy/Net7.cpp` constructs `udp_to_global` with `unconnected=true`; `proxy/UDPClient.{h,cpp}` ctor takes optional `unconnected` flag stored in `m_Unconnected`; `proxy/UDPClient_linux.cpp` OpenFixedPort gates connect() on `!m_Unconnected`, UDP_RecvFromServer branches on m_Unconnected to recvfrom + IP whitelist, UDP_Send port==0 branches on m_Unconnected to sendto m_SockAddr. `proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp` activates the global plane on master-handoff confirm and flips LoginComplete on START_ACK so its SendPacketSequence early-return doesn't gate in-game frames. `proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp` HandleStageConfirm forwards exactly 4 bytes (int32_t stage_wire) instead of 8 (sizeof(long)). (c) **sizeof(long) wire-size sweep across server** — `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp` SendOpcode + SendLoginStageConfirm + HandleLoginAckReturn + SendStart + admin Terminate + SendTalkTreeAction + LOOT_HULK_PERMISSION all use int32_t; `server/src/PlayerClass.cpp` SendShipDataToSelf + SendShipData self-branch use int32_t game_id_wire; `server/src/PlayerManager.cpp` force-terminate uses int32_t player_id, and GetPlayer mask widened from `& 0x00FFFFFF` (silently capping at 24 bits) to `~(PLAYER_TAG | MANU_TAG)`; `server/src/UDP_Master.cpp` ProcessHandoff passes int32_t game_id to AddData. `server/src/SectorData.h` IS_PLAYER macro: dropped the bogus `< 0xFFFFF` upper bound that was rejecting every char-based GameID (CharID = account_id*5+slot+1 routinely exceeds 1M; e.g. account 9000001 slot 0 → CharID 45000006). The PLAYER_TAG bit alone is the canonical check, matching the macro's name.
      Bonus fixes that landed alongside: **Phase N MySQL stored-proc inlining** — `accLogin`/`avaLogin`/`avaLogout`/`incWarn`/`logoutOnShutdown` were silent no-ops since libpqxx can't load MySQL DELIMITER blocks; bodies inlined in SaveManager/AccountManager/ServerManager per `db/postgres/seed.sql` source; schema qualifier `net7_user.` stripped from all UPDATEs. **`fflush(stdout)`** after every LogMessage/LogMySQLMsg so `docker compose logs server` sees output in real time (was block-buffered without a TTY → debugging took ~10x longer than necessary). **TlsLoginTests.ValidAccount_ReturnsValidTicket** flaky-assertion fixed (asserted `Length >= 20` against `LinuxAuth.cpp` ticket format `%s-%d` which is 12-21 chars for cli_test01; replaced with `StartsWith(username + "-")` + digit suffix check; comment claimed "40-character hex ticket" the code never emitted).
      Touches: `proxy/Net7.cpp`, `proxy/UDPClient.{h,cpp}`, `proxy/UDPClient_linux.cpp`, `proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp`, `proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp`, `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp`, `server/src/PlayerClass.cpp`, `server/src/PlayerManager.cpp`, `server/src/UDP_Master.cpp`, `server/src/SectorData.h`, `server/src/SaveManager.cpp`, `server/src/AccountManager.cpp`, `server/src/SectorContentSQL.cpp`, `server/src/ServerManager.cpp`, `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/ServerFixture.cs` (WaitForServerSectorAsync polls docker logs for `BeginSectorThread sector_id=10151` marker), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorLoginTests.cs` (new, ~444 LOC), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Handshake/TlsLoginTests.cs` (ticket assertion fix), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0005/+0x2020/+0x2021).
      Notes: end-to-end happy path is now green. Next-Phase-K work is broader opcode coverage (sector enumerate / inventory / movement / chat at sector scope), not handshake plumbing. See decisions log entry 2026-05-25 "Phase K sector LOGIN round-trip GREEN".

- [x] Wave 8 (2026-05-25): first post-START sector opcode — 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT Group/no-group round-trip.
      Status: done — `SectorChatTests.GroupChat_WhenUngrouped_ReceivesNotInGroupErrorString` passes in 7s; full 40-test integration suite passes in 3m6s. Exercises the entire server→client server-side opcode pipeline that every in-sector reply rides: `Player::HandleClientChat` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:4544) → `Type==1` branch → `GroupID()==-1` check → `SendVaMessage("Error: You are not in a group!")` → `Player::SendMessageString` (PlayerConnection.cpp:10918) → `SendOpcode(0x001D)` → `m_UDPQueue` → `SendPacketCache` → 0x2016 PACKET_SEQUENCE on UDP → proxy `UDPClient::SendClientPacketSequence` (proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:531) → 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING on sector TCP 3500. The Group/no-group branch chosen because it is the simplest server-state-independent path that produces a deterministic single-frame reply (slash-commands require GM permissions, broadcast requires another receiver, target/local/guild need extra state; "not in a group" only depends on the default `GroupID()==-1`).

SectorLoginTests is now ~95 LOC orchestration over the helper. - [x] Wave 9 (2026-05-25): second post-START sector opcode — 0x0044 REQUEST_TIME → 0x0034 CLIENT_SET_TIME round-trip, with the predicted `sizeof(long)` over-read fix to `Player::HandleRequestTime` **and** a latent `AuxBase::m_Max_Buffer` uninit bug that the test surfaced.
      Status: done — `SectorRequestTimeTests.RequestTime_RoundTripsClientSentTickAndReturnsServerTimes` passes in 7s; full 41-test integration suite green in 3m17s. Exercises the simplest possible in-sector request/reply pair (HandleRequestTime is unconditional — no player-state guards) and asserts that the server echoes the client's exact tick back as `ClientSent`, which is a positive correlation signal: a wire-size or byte-order bug at the server would put garbage in that slot. Client sentinel chosen as `(int)(DateTime.UtcNow.Ticks & 0x7FFFFFFF)` so a leaked-recv-buffer regression can't accidentally echo a matching value run-to-run.
      Server fix 1 — `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:1624` `*((long *) data)` → `*((int32_t *) data)` — same class of bug as the Wave 7 sweep. Win32 wire payload is 4 bytes (a single `long` = 4 on Win32), but the unmigrated Linux server read `*((long *) data)` which is 8 bytes — pulling 4B of payload plus 4B of whatever followed it in the recv buffer, then echoing that garbage back to the client as its own `ClientSent` tick. Test would have failed on the `Assert.Equal(clientTick, echoedClientSent)` line. The `ClientSetTime` struct itself (`common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:563`) was already migrated to `int32_t` in Wave 7, so the wire size on the reply side (12B) was already correct — only the request-side read was wrong.
      Server fix 2 — `server/src/AuxClasses/AuxBase.cpp` `AuxBase::AuxBase()` now sets `m_Max_Buffer = (unsigned long)-1`. Test surfaced this: SectorRequestTime in isolation passed, but failed in the 3-test sector sequence (SectorLogin → SectorChat → SectorRequestTime) with OperationCanceledException — server log showed thousands of `Error: Bufferoverflow in Aux!` printf bursts and zero `Received RequestTime` entries. Root cause: only 4 of 57 `AuxBase` subclasses (`AuxHulkIndex=1000`, `AuxShipIndex=10000`, `AuxMobIndex=2000`, `AuxHarvestable=2000`) explicitly set `m_Max_Buffer`. The other 53 leave it uninitialised. On Win32 the heap garbage happened to be large enough that `AddData()`'s `sizeof(T)+index < m_Max_Buffer` guard passed through; on Linux the garbage is often small, so every `AddData()` call hits the printf branch. With 3+ players in the same sector, the per-player serialisation flood saturates stdout and stalls the sector tick — REQUEST_TIME never reaches `HandleRequestTime`. The fix initialises `m_Max_Buffer` to `ULONG_MAX` in the base constructor, restoring Win32 de-facto behaviour without weakening any actual bound (the load-bearing safety mechanism is caller-side buffer sizing, not this check; the four subclasses that *know* a tighter cap keep their explicit assignments and override the default).
      Touches: `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp` (HandleRequestTime sizeof(long) fix), `server/src/AuxClasses/AuxBase.cpp` (m_Max_Buffer default), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorRequestTimeTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[5] cli_test06 to avoid colliding with SectorLoginTests' Pool[3] and SectorChatTests' Pool[4]; 90s budget; 200-frame drain cap; xmldoc records all three failure classes including the AuxBase suite-state regression), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test06 entry), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test06 INSERT row; comments updated 9000005→9000006 and "all five"→"all six"), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0034 ClientSetTime, +0x0044 RequestTime), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 17→19; entries for 0x0034 CLIENT_SET_TIME and 0x0044 REQUEST_TIME).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet: 17/207 → 19/207 (9.2%). The HarnessSmokeTest `SeedSql_IsCopiedToOutput_AndMentionsEveryPooledAccount` iterates Pool dynamically so the new 6th account is picked up without test code changes. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: the `m_Max_Buffer` fix is preservation-aligned (restores 15+ years of upstream behaviour by initialising what was uninitialised — Win32 happened to have large garbage there) and does not loosen any real bound. Next-Phase-K targets: 0x0006 START_ACK closure (SetActive(true) gates Active() checks for movement/inventory), 0x0012 TURN and 0x0013 TILT (simplest movement opcodes — fan-out across sector players is the new path), 0x002C ACTION (combat trigger).

- [x] Wave 17 (2026-05-25): 0x0057 SKILL_UP survival round-trip — untrained skill for the avatar's profession trips the "already maxed" early return (Level=0 == MaxSkillLevel=0).
      Status: done — `SectorSkillUpTests.SkillUp_OnUntrainedSkill_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes; full integration suite green from the running stack. Zero-server-change wave — Phase R already had SkillAction canonical as `{int32_t GameID; int SkillPoints; short SkillID;}` = 10B (common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:987; `int` is 4B on both Win32 and Linux x86_64 so the struct width is invariant across platforms). SKILL_UP (0x0057) is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so it hits the `default:` arm at line 514 and falls through to bottom-of-switch `g_ServerMgr->m_UDPConnection->ForwardClientOpcode(...)`. Server-side `Player::HandleSkillAction` (server/src/PlayerSkills.cpp:97) has three early-return guards before any state mutation: (1) `SkillLevel == SkillMaxLevel` (already maxed); (2) insufficient skill points; (3) `SkillLevelRequirement > 0` (prereq skill not high enough). For a SkillID valid in the AuxSkills wrapper but untrained for the avatar's class, the first guard trips on `0 == 0` and the handler returns silently — no DB write, no AuxPlayer/AuxShip refresh, no reply. Pipe survival is the only assertable post-condition (matches Waves 10/11/13/14/15/16 pattern).
      SkillID choice — **and the trap we walked into**: initial draft sent SkillID=169 reasoning from `_Skills::Skill[170]` (server/src/AuxClasses/AuxSkills.h:23-26, the raw data array). **This crashed the sector thread** because the dispatcher path indexes through `m_PlayerIndex.RPGInfo.Skills.Skill[Action->SkillID]` where `RPGInfo.Skills` is `class AuxSkills` (AuxRPGInfo.h:134), whose `Skill` member is **`AuxSkill Skill[64]`** (AuxSkills.h:86) — the wrapper array is only 64 entries, not 170. `AuxSkills::Init` confirms it only loops `i<64` (AuxSkills.h:64-67). Any SkillID ≥ 64 dereferences past the wrapper array end into Player-object memory, reads a garbage `_Skill * Data` pointer, and `GetAvailability()` faults the sector thread (verified via `docker inspect enb-emulator-server-1 --format '{{.RestartCount}}'` = 2 with StartedAt jumping to the same second the bad SKILL_UP frame was sent). Corrected SkillID to **29 SKILL_JENQUAI_CULTURE** — per the seeded Postgres `skills` table, `warrior_max_level = -1` for that row, so the per-profession init loop in PlayerSaves::LoadPlayer (server/src/PlayerSaves.cpp:609-647) skips the entry (`Skills[29].ClassType[0].MaxLevel` stays ≤ 0) and `RPGInfo.Skills.Skill[29]` keeps the AuxSkill::Init defaults (Level=0, MaxSkillLevel=0, Availability[3]=0). First early-return fires, pipe survives.
      Regression coverage — if anyone reverts SkillAction's `int SkillPoints` to `long SkillPoints`, the struct grows from 10B to 14B on Linux x86_64: SkillID would read from byte 12 (instead of 8), past the end of the 10B wire payload, into undefined memory. A garbage SkillID < 64 would index a random AuxSkill wrapper slot — could trip into the mutation path on the wrong skill, corrupting player state. A garbage SkillID ≥ 64 would crash the sector thread on the OOB Data-pointer deref (the same crash that bit the initial test). Also catches: proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode regression (drops the opcode); m_Mutex deadlock if a regression moves the lock above the early-return guards; dispatcher mis-route at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:499 (hand-maintained ~200-entry switch); AuxSkills::Init loop-bound shrinking below 30 (the Jenquai-Culture pick at 29 is inside the current `<64` bound, but a regression shrinking it to 32 would crash on Jenquai-Culture too).
      Server-side bounds gap left for future hardening — `PlayerSkills.cpp:101` has no `if (Action->SkillID < 0 || Action->SkillID >= 64) return;` guard before the OOB-prone indexing. The real Win32 client never sends SkillID ≥ 64 (UI only surfaces trainable skills, all in [0..57] per the SkillNames[64] table at PlayerSkills.cpp:37-95), so retail wire never tripped it — it's an existing latent gap, not a regression. Per CLAUDE.md "tightening the server toward greater fidelity is always welcome", a defensive bounds guard would be a legitimate hardening but is intentionally NOT bundled into this wave (scope = exercise the round-trip; the right fix is a `static constexpr int kMaxSkills = 64;` in AuxSkills.h used both for the array decl and the bounds check, and probably part of a broader sweep of similar dispatcher reads). Documented in plans/99-decisions-log.md 2026-05-25 for future contributors.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorSkillUpTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[12] cli_test14 to avoid colliding with Pool[3..11]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents survival-probe rationale, the AuxSkills::Skill[64] vs _Skills::Skill[170] trap and prior bad reasoning, the SkillID=29 Jenquai-on-Terran-Warrior rationale via skills.warrior_max_level=-1, sizeof(long) SkillAction regression class, proxy default-case fragility, m_Mutex deadlock + dispatcher mis-route + AuxSkills::Init bound hazards, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that the SKILL_UP click is a published retail action), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test14 entry — 9_000_014), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test14 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0057 SkillUp in sorted position between 0x004E StarbaseRequest and 0x006D GlobalConnect), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 26→27; sorted-position entry for 0x0057 SKILL_UP between 0x004E STARBASE_REQUEST and 0x006D GLOBAL_CONNECT).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet 26/207 → 27/207 (13.0%). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; the SKILL_UP click on an untrained skill is exactly what the retail Win32 client emits and the retail server's no-op silent-return is faithfully preserved. Next-Phase-K targets: 0x005A VERB_REQUEST (NPC talk-tree exercise — could pair with action=4 STARBASE_REQUEST once we have a seed NPC); 0x0011 NAV (in-flight nav target selection — natural follow-on to MOVE); 0x002F BUY_ITEM (vendor purchase — pure server state mutator on inventory).

Server-side `Player::HandleVerbRequest` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:3547) is short — reads SubjectID/ObjectID via ntohl(), checks `subject_id == GameID() && pkt->Action == 1`, and on mismatch returns silently. We send SubjectID=0; cli_test15's GameID (assigned by SaveManager as `account_id*5 + slot + 1`) is non-zero, so the equality test fails and the handler exits without entering UpdateVerbs.       Why a survival probe — even on a SubjectID match, `UpdateVerbs(true)` (server/src/PlayerClass.cpp:3500) early-returns when `GetObjectFromID(GetTargetGameID())` returns null (no targeted object), which is exactly the post-handshake state for a freshly-created character. No reply on either branch. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules we don't fabricate one.
      Full-suite re-run gotcha — running SectorVerbRequestTests in isolation first, *then* re-running the full suite (without recycling the docker stack) produced `Failed: 1, Passed: 48` with `G_ERROR_ACCOUNT_IN_USE (code=13)` from cli_test15 at SectorHandshake.cs:89 — the prior isolated invocation left cli_test15 marked active on the global server. Fix: `docker compose down -v && docker compose up -d` between runs cleans the global session state. The full suite green from a fresh stack is the authoritative verification. (Future hardening: the test's `finally` block could explicitly log the account off before deleting the character, instead of relying on session expiry. Out of scope for this wave.)
      Regression coverage — if anyone reverts VerbRequest's three int32_t fields to long, the struct grows from 12B to 16B/20B/24B on Linux x86_64: Action would read from byte 16 (instead of 8), past the end of the 12B wire payload into undefined memory, mis-comparing against the `Action == 1` guard at minimum. SubjectID=0 is a fixed point under byte-swap so ntohl regressions on SubjectID itself wouldn't surface here — but a regression that dropped ntohl on a non-zero SubjectID would suddenly hit (or miss) the GameID-equality branch on the wrong endianness. Also catches: proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode regression (drops the opcode); dispatcher mis-route at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:507 (hand-maintained ~200-entry switch); null-deref regression in the equality short-circuit (current code reads both subject_id and object_id from the wire before the equality check).

- [x] Wave 19 (2026-05-25): 0x0017 REQUEST_TARGET direct-reply round-trip — null-target request reaches `Player::HandleRequestTarget` which unconditionally emits 0x0019 SET_TARGET with the hard-coded `-1` sentinel TargetID. **First direct-reply correlation in Phase K post-Wave-9** (Waves 10/11/13/14/15/16/17/18 were all survival probes).
      Status: done — `SectorRequestTargetTests.RequestTarget_OnNullTarget_ReceivesSetTargetWithSentinelTargetIdMinusOne` passes in isolation (1/1, 7s) AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack (50/50, 2m25s). Zero-server-change wave — Phase R already had RequestTarget canonical as `{int32_t GameID; int32_t TargetID;}` = 8B (common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:528) and SetTarget canonical with the same shape (PacketStructures.h:540). REQUEST_TARGET is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so it hits the `default:` arm at line 514 and falls through to bottom-of-switch `ForwardClientOpcode(...)`. Server-side `Player::HandleRequestTarget` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:3390) **unconditionally** calls `SendSetTarget(request->TargetID, -1)` regardless of whether the requested target exists — `GetObjectFromID(0)` returns null for both newtarget and oldtarget, `m_ProspectWindow` is false on a fresh starbase character so the OpenInterface branch is skipped, SendSetTarget fires, then `BlankVerbs()` (PlayerClass.cpp:3467 = safe memset) runs and the threat-rank logic at the bottom is gated on `newtarget != null` so it's skipped. This is the **first post-Wave-9 direct-reply opcode** — Waves 10/11/13/14/15/16/17/18 were all survival probes because their handlers either no-op'd, fanned out only to OTHER players, or guarded on player state we couldn't satisfy.
      Why a direct-reply assertion beats a survival probe — survival probes ("pipe still alive") prove the handler didn't crash but say nothing about correctness. Direct-reply with a known sentinel (`-1`) **plus** a known mirror (`GameID == request->TargetID == 0`) **plus** a known payload size (8B) gives three positive-correlation signals in one test. A regression that swapped the SetTarget GameID/TargetID field order would silently break (positive: replyTargetID=-1 would appear in the GameID slot). A regression that widened either field to long would balloon the reply to 12B or 16B (positive: payload length assertion fails immediately). A regression in the server→client UDP fan-out path that affected only this opcode on a sub-branch of `SendClientPacketSequence` framing logic (proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:531) would surface as a timeout here even though Wave 8's MESSAGE_STRING still passed.
      Full-suite re-run gotcha recurrence — same ACCOUNT_IN_USE-on-re-run pattern as Wave 18: running SectorRequestTargetTests in isolation, then re-running the full suite without recycling the docker stack produced `G_ERROR_ACCOUNT_IN_USE (code=13)` for cli_test16. Fix: `docker compose down -v && docker compose up -d` between runs. This is now the **second wave** to hit this pattern, suggesting a wave-N+1 hardening opportunity: the test's `finally` block could explicitly send `0x0003 LOGOFF` (or whatever the global plane logoff sequence is) before deleting the character, instead of relying on session expiry. Filed as future hardening; out of scope for Wave 19.
      Regression coverage — if anyone reverts RequestTarget's `int32_t GameID/TargetID` to long, the struct grows from 8B to 12B/16B on Linux x86_64: TargetID would read from byte 8 (past the end of the 8B wire payload) into undefined memory, then **walk the threat-rank path on a stale newtarget pointer** which could crash. If SetTarget reply is widened to long, the assertion that payload length is exactly 8 catches it immediately. If the SetTarget struct fields are reordered (GameID/TargetID swap), our assert `replyTargetID == -1` fails (the literal -1 would appear in the GameID slot instead). Also catches: proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode regression (drops the opcode → timeout); server→client UDP fan-out regression in SendClientPacketSequence framing on a sub-branch unique to this opcode (timeout); dispatcher mis-route at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:443 (hand-maintained ~200-entry switch); BlankVerbs/SetTargetGameID introducing a crash hazard.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorRequestTargetTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[14] cli_test16 to avoid colliding with Pool[3..13]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents direct-reply rationale, full HandleRequestTarget code path walk-through, GameID/TargetID mirror semantics, 6 regression classes with primary-source citations, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that TargetID=0 is exactly what the retail Win32 client emits when the user clicks empty space to clear the active target, and the unconditional SetTarget(-1) reply is the faithful retail behaviour — the -1 sentinel means "no rank/threat info yet"), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test16 entry — 9_000_016), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test16 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0017 RequestTarget and +0x0019 SetTarget in sorted position between 0x0014 Move and 0x001D MessageString), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 28→30; sorted-position entries for 0x0017 REQUEST_TARGET and 0x0019 SET_TARGET between 0x0014 MOVE and 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING).

Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; the REQUEST_TARGET-with-TargetID=0 wire shape is byte-identical to what the retail Win32 client emits when the user clicks empty space; the unconditional SetTarget reply with TargetID=-1 is the faithful retail behaviour. - [x] Wave 61 (2026-05-27): 0x0065 UI_TRIGGER (`/uitrigger 0,0` CLIENT_CHAT slash command at PlayerConnection.cpp:7575-7592) **second indirect-stimulus +1 ratchet** — thirty-first direct/indirect-reply wave. +1 ratchet 95/207 → **96/207 (46.4%)**.
      Status: done — `SectorUiTriggerTests.UiTriggerSlashCommand_OnSlashUitrigger_ReceivesUiTriggerEmit` written; build green; test passes (8s); zero server change.
      Pattern — client establishes a station-sector handshake at Luna Station (sector 10151) and sends a 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT carrying Message="/uitrigger 0,0", Type=Group. `Player::HandleClientChat` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:4614) forwards to `HandleSlashCommands`'s single-slash block at PlayerConnection.cpp:5447. The case 'u' arm at PlayerConnection.cpp:7575-7592 matches `MatchOptWithParam("uitrigger", pch, param, msg_sent)` (the first arm in case 'u'; `else if (MatchOptWithParam("upgrade", ...))` follows but only triggers on string "upgrade" which differs from "uitrigger" at position 1). `strtok_s` pulls a="0" and b="0"; on `if (b)` true the handler runs `int Index=0; unsigned char Data[75]; *((long*) &Data[Index]) = atoi(a); Index+=4; *((long*) &Data[Index]) = atoi(b); Index+=4; SendOpcode(ENB_OPCODE_0065_UI_TRIGGER, &Data, Index=8)`. Wire payload Index=8 bytes: {int32 a; int32 b} little-endian. For a=0, b=0 the payload is 8 zero bytes.
      Test — new `UiTriggerSlashCommand_OnSlashUitrigger_ReceivesUiTriggerEmit` in `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorUiTriggerTests.cs`. Single-stage `EstablishAsync` at sectorId=10151; stimulus 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT with Message="/uitrigger 0,0", Type=Group followed by 400-frame drain for 0x0065 asserts payload.Length EXACTLY 8, bytes[0..4]==0 (a echo), bytes[4..8]==0 (b echo). Cleanup runs explicit 0x00B9 → 0x00BA logoff + `GlobalDeleteCharacter` (identical pattern to Waves 55-60).
      Legitimacy — second indirect-stimulus wave in Phase K (Wave 60 was the first via /openif). Slash-command dispatcher and the /uitrigger SendOpcode site exist in the upstream server; Wave 61 pins existing behaviour with zero server change, zero widened input acceptance, zero loosened gating, zero debug-only opcode. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rule, exactly the "tightening" the rule welcomes. **The sizeof(long) WRITE-path bug at PlayerConnection.cpp:7585/7587 is wire-invisible here, unlike Wave 59's HandleCTARequest**. On Linux x86_64 the first 8B write to Data[0..8] stores low 4B=atoi(a) and high 4B=0; the second 8B write to Data[4..12] overwrites Data[4..8] with low 4B=atoi(b) and stores high 4B=0 at Data[8..12]; the final SendOpcode(... Index=8) only emits Data[0..8] = {a, b} which is identical to clean int32_t* writes, and the 75B buffer prevents stack overflow. This is the **third leg of the Phase K sizeof(long) bug taxonomy**: (1) READ over-read (Waves 7/11/12); (2) WRITE buffer overflow clobbering adjacent fields (Wave 59 — HandleCTARequest with 9B stack array); (3) WRITE wire-invisible-but-fragile (Wave 61 — fortunate-accident wire shape pinned so any future surrounding-code change surfaces).
      Regression coverage — 10 classes documented inline in test xmldoc and TestedOpcodes commentary: (a) 0x0065 emit removal at PlayerConnection.cpp:7589; (b) sizeof(long) WRITE-path regression flipping wire-visibility — widening emit slice to Index=16, reordering b-then-a so the high-half clobber goes the wrong direction, or dropping Index+=4 increments so both writes land at Data[0] — all surface via 8B length assertion or {a,b} value assertions; (c) single-slash gate regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:5447; (d) case 'u' dispatch regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:7575; (e) MatchOptWithParam parsing regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:4526-4554; (f) strtok_s second-call regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:7578-7579 — if b comes back NULL the SendOpcode is skipped and drain times out; (g) HandleClientChat slash dispatch regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:4614-4617; (h) ClientChatCodec wire-format regression; (i) proxy SendClientPacketSequence inner-opcode guard at UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:568 tightening (0x0065 < 0x0FFF currently passes); (j) SendOpcode header-width revert at PlayerConnection.cpp:127.
      Seam-discovery — Wave 61 establishes the indirect-stimulus pattern as a **repeatable** category, not a one-off. The /uitrigger arm has the same shape as the /openif arm except the SendOpcode wraps the args directly (no helper-function intermediary like Player::OpenInterface) — confirming the pattern generalises across single-slash arms. Wave 61 also **identifies the third leg of the Phase K sizeof(long) bug taxonomy** — wire-invisible-but-fragile WRITE paths where the source-level bug exists but the wire shape happens to be correct by a combination of buffer width and trailing-overwrite arrangement. This is more dangerous than the Wave-59 class because it's invisible until someone refactors the surrounding code — a pure preservation hazard that Wave 61's test now pins. A grep audit of `\*((long\*) &.*\[Index\]\) = atoi` patterns in server/src/ would enumerate other Wave-61-class sites worth pinning. Future indirect-stimulus candidates (still): /panup, /panx, /pany, /music, /move, /noattack, /notells, /level — many require AdminLevel >= GM which cli_test* seed accounts (status=100=ADMIN) clear; a couple require non-fresh-character state (group membership, target lock, prospect window) and are deferred.

      Status: done — `SectorOpenInterfaceTests.OpenInterfaceSlashCommand_OnSlashOpenif_ReceivesOpenInterfaceEmit` written; build green; test passes (7s); zero server change.
      Pattern — client establishes a station-sector handshake at Luna Station (sector 10151) and sends a 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT carrying Message="/openif 0,0", Type=Group. `Player::HandleClientChat` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:4614) checks `chat->String[0] == '/'` and forwards to `Player::HandleSlashCommands` (PlayerConnection.cpp:4682). HandleSlashCommands has two top-level if-blocks: the GM/double-slash block at PlayerConnection.cpp:4716 (gated on `Msg[0]=='/' && Msg[1]=='/' && Msg[2]!=0 && AdminLevel() >= GM`) and the normal single-slash block at PlayerConnection.cpp:5447 (gated on `Msg[0]=='/' && Msg[1]!=0 && (!msg_sent || !success)`). The GM switch only has cases a,b,c,d,e,f,h,k,r,s,w,g — there is no case 'o'. The `openif` arm at PlayerConnection.cpp:6885-6905 lives inside the SECOND switch's case 'o', so single-slash `/openif` is the correct stimulus: `Msg[1]='o'` fails the GM gate's double-slash check, the message falls into the single-slash block with `pch="openif 0,0"`, `*pch='o'`, and the second switch dispatches case 'o'. The case 'o' arm chain runs strcmp("ori") → MatchOptWithParam("orientation") → MatchOptWithParam("oeuler") → MatchOptWithParam("openif"); the openif arm matches because `strncmp("openif", "openif 0,0", 6)==0` and `arg[6]==' '` sets `param="0,0"`. Then `strtok_s(param, ",", &next_token)` pulls `a="0"`, a second `strtok_s(NULL, ",", &next_token)` pulls `b="0"`, and on `if (b)` true the handler calls `OpenInterface(atoi(a), atoi(b))` + `SendVaMessage("OpenInterface (%d,%d):", atoi(a), atoi(b))`. `Player::OpenInterface` (PlayerConnection.cpp:3576-3584) fills a stack-local `SetInterface` struct `{int32_t UIChange; int32_t UIType}` (common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:534-538) from the two arguments and emits via `SendOpcode(ENB_OPCODE_0066_OPEN_INTERFACE, &set_interface, sizeof(set_interface)=8)`. For UIChange=0, UIType=0 the wire payload is exactly 8 bytes of zeros.
      Test — new `OpenInterfaceSlashCommand_OnSlashOpenif_ReceivesOpenInterfaceEmit` in `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorOpenInterfaceTests.cs`. Single-stage `EstablishAsync` at sectorId=10151 lands the avatar in Luna Station; stimulus 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT with Message="/openif 0,0", Type=Group followed by 400-frame drain for 0x0066 asserts payload.Length EXACTLY 8, bytes[0..4]==0 (UIChange echo), bytes[4..8]==0 (UIType echo). Cleanup runs explicit 0x00B9 LOGOFF_REQUEST → 0x00BA LOGOFF_CONFIRMATION round-trip + `GlobalDeleteCharacter` on global TCP (identical pattern to Waves 55-59).
      Legitimacy — Wave 60 introduces the **first indirect-stimulus pattern** to the Phase K catalogue: the client sends one opcode (0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT) and asserts on a different server-emit opcode (0x0066 OPEN_INTERFACE) by virtue of the slash-command dispatcher. The slash-command dispatcher and the OpenInterface call site exist in the upstream server unchanged; Wave 60 pins existing behaviour with zero server change, zero widened input acceptance, zero loosened gating, zero debug-only opcode. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rule, the test simply drives an existing server-emit path with valid client stimulus — exactly the "tightening" the rule welcomes.
      Regression coverage — 10 classes documented inline in test xmldoc and TestedOpcodes commentary: (a) 0x0066 emit removal at PlayerConnection.cpp:3583 — drain times out; (b) SetInterface wire-layout regression at PacketStructures.h:534-538 — widening either field to `long` on Linux x86_64 grows payload to 12B/16B and the length assertion catches; (c) Player::OpenInterface signature regression — function takes `long UIChange, long UIType` at PlayerConnection.cpp:3576 but SetInterface fields are int32_t at line 537, implicit narrowing is one-way truncation; refactor swapping assignment direction or widening struct fields would surface; (d) single-slash gate regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:5447 — refactor tightening to double-slash, adding AdminLevel check, or rejecting Msg[1]='o' kills the test; (e) case 'o' dispatch regression in the single-slash switch (PlayerConnection.cpp:6885) — switch label removal or earlier MatchOptWithParam in case 'o' eating the "openif" prefix; (f) MatchOptWithParam parsing regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:4526-4554 — splits on `=` or ` `; narrowing separator set (e.g. `=`-only) stops parsing "openif 0,0"; (g) strtok_s second-call regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:6887-6888 — if `b` comes back NULL the `if (b)` guard skips OpenInterface entirely; (h) HandleClientChat slash dispatch regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:4614-4617 — slash check (`chat->String[0] == '/'`) must fire BEFORE the Type-dependent branches; refactor moving check below Type=Group branch re-routes our chat into "You are not in a group!" error path; (i) ClientChatCodec wire-format regression — int32_t GameID + char Type + short Size + char[] String NUL-terminated; EncodeOutbound miscomputing Size or dropping NUL terminator mis-parses ClientChat struct; (j) proxy SendClientPacketSequence inner-opcode guard at proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:568 tightening (currently passes 0x0066 < 0x0FFF) + SendOpcode header-width revert at PlayerConnection.cpp:127.

      Pattern — client establishes a station-sector handshake at Luna Station (sector 10151) and sends a 12-byte 0x00BC CTA_REQUEST packed struct `{int32 SourceID=0x12345678; int32 TargetID=0; int32 Action=0}`. Server `Player::HandleCTARequest` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:7723-7744) calls `PlayerManager::GroupAction(SourceID, TargetID, Action)` which dispatches on `(Action - 4)` with cases 0..8 (Action values 4..12 fan out to `SetFormation`/`FormUp`/`RequestTargetMyTarget` per the binary disasm of `PlayerManager::GroupAction` at libnet7-server `PlayerManager::GroupAction(long,long,long)`); `Action=0` forces the default arm — a logging no-op that returns without dereferencing `SourceID`/`TargetID`. Then `HandleCTARequest` unconditionally emits 0x00BD CTA_RESPONSE via `SendOpcode(ENB_OPCODE_00BD_CTA_RESPONSE, &CTAResponse, sizeof(CTAResponse)=9)` with our `SourceID` and `Action` echoed back via two pointer-cast assignments at PlayerConnection.cpp:7740-7741.
      Test — new `CtaRequest_OnDefaultArmAction_ReceivesCtaResponseWithSuccessByte` in `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorCtaRequestTests.cs`. Single-stage `EstablishAsync` at sectorId=10151 lands the avatar in Luna Station; stimulus 12-byte CTA_REQUEST with `Action=0` followed by 400-frame drain for 0x00BD asserts payload.Length EXACTLY 9, bytes[0..4]==SourceID (0x12345678 LE), bytes[4..8]==Action (0x00000000 LE), and bytes[8]==0x01 (Success). Cleanup runs explicit 0x00B9 LOGOFF_REQUEST → 0x00BA LOGOFF_CONFIRMATION round-trip + `GlobalDeleteCharacter` on global TCP (identical pattern to Waves 55-58).
      Legitimacy — direct-reply round-trip on a server-originated reply opcode the real retail server always produced on the real retail client's group-action UI commit ("Call To Arms" per the inline handler comment at PlayerConnection.cpp:7722). **Server tightening landed in this wave**: pre-fix the response-buffer construction at PlayerConnection.cpp:7740-7741 was `*((long*) &CTAResponse[0]) = myCTARequest->SourceID;` and `*((long*) &CTAResponse[4]) = myCTARequest->Action;` — on Win32 retail `sizeof(long)==4` made each write 4B and exactly fit the 9-byte `CTAResponse` stack array (4B SourceID + 4B Action + 1B Success), but on Linux x86_64 `sizeof(long)==8` made the second write overflow [4..12] by 3 bytes AND clobber the Success byte at [8] with the sign-extended high byte of `Action` (0x00 for any non-negative Action, 0xFF for negative). Wave 59 narrows both writes to `int32_t*` — restores retail's 4-byte semantics AND eliminates the 3-byte stack overflow. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rule, this is preservation-grade fidelity tightening (Win32 retail's `sizeof(long)==4` made the original writes correct on the platform retail ran on; Wave 59 restores that semantic on Linux x86_64) — exactly the "tightening" the rule welcomes. Zero widened input acceptance, zero loosened gating, zero permissiveness.
      Regression coverage — 10 classes documented inline in test xmldoc and TestedOpcodes commentary: (a) **the Phase K long→int32_t tightening regression at PlayerConnection.cpp:7740-7741** — a revert reintroduces the 3-byte stack overflow AND clobbers Success to 0x00 (for Action=0); byte-exact Success==0x01 assertion catches directly; (b) HandleCTARequest case-0x00BC branch deletion at PlayerConnection.cpp:595-596 (drain times out); (c) SendOpcode opcode-id flip at the emit site (typo from `ENB_OPCODE_00BD_CTA_RESPONSE` to a neighbour); (d) the 9-byte `sizeof(CTAResponse)` emit-length pin — a refactor widening the array or shifting the emit boundary surfaces as != 9B; (e) CTARequest struct layout regression at common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:974-979 (12B canonical, 3× int32_t ATTRIB_PACKED; long-revert on any field shifts the others — byte-exact echo asserts catch); (f) PlayerManager::GroupAction dispatch-table corruption — the (Action-4) switch's default arm is a logging no-op, any refactor adding a side effect (DB write, fan-out, crash on null target) under the default arm surfaces as either different reply opcode count or session crash; (g) GroupAction null-pointer regression on null source/target player lookups — Action=0 forces default arm BEFORE any player lookup, refactor moving lookup to function entry crashes on bogus SourceID/TargetID; (h) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping 0x00BC (not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so relies on bottom-of-switch fallthrough); (i) SendOpcode header-width revert at PlayerConnection.cpp:127; (j) proxy SendClientPacketSequence inner-opcode guard at proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:568 tightening (currently passes 0x00BD < 0x0FFF).
      Seam-discovery — Wave 59 introduces a NEW Phase K seam class: **"server reply field clobbered by sizeof(long) stack overflow"**. Prior Phase K sizeof(long) fixes (Waves 7/11/12) targeted client→server READ paths (struct over-reads past wire-payload end). Wave 59 is the first to target a server→client WRITE path (response-buffer overflow corrupting an adjacent field within the same emit). Future audits of `*((long*) &buf[N])`-style writes anywhere in `server/src/` should treat this pattern as the third leg of the Phase K sizeof(long) bug taxonomy: (1) READ over-read past wire-payload end into garbage (Waves 7/11/12); (2) WRITE past response-buffer end clobbering adjacent stack/heap (Wave 59 — the new class). A grep audit of `\*((long\*)` across server/src/ should be the next post-Wave-59 prep step to enumerate other sites. Next-Phase-K targets after Wave 59: grep audit for `\*((long\*)` writes anywhere in server/src/ + auto-test+fix any further sites surfaced; case-8 `sizeof(long)` server-fidelity tightening at PlayerConnection.cpp:10005 (Linux x86_64 sizeof(long)==8 vs retail Win32's 4 — would also pin 0x0096 with byte-exact 4B payload; pre-existing Wave 57/58 target); 0x004F STARBASE_SET negative-assertion wave on the space-sector handshake; upgrade existing 28+ survival-probe assertions to byte-exact reply-shape assertions.

- [x] Wave 52 (2026-05-27): 0x003C CLIENT_TYPE + 0x0097 GALAXY_MAP (`SectorManager::SectorLogin` SPACE-sector emits) **passive-observation +2 ratchet** via NEW 2-stage station→space login pattern. +2 ratchet 82/207 → **84/207 (40.6%)**.
      Status: done — `SectorHandshakeFanoutTests.HandshakeEmitsClientTypeAndGalaxyMapOnSpaceSectorLogin` written; build green; test passes 1/1 in 11s.
      Pattern — captures two opcodes that ONLY emit on the SPACE-sector branch of the sector-login dispatch. `SectorManager::HandleSectorLogin` at `server/src/SectorManager.cpp:324-336` routes `m_SectorID > 9999` to `StationLogin` (line 328) and the else-branch to `SectorLogin` (line 332). Every prior handshake-fanout wave uses `sectorId=10151` (Luna Station, `m_SectorID > 9999`) which hits StationLogin — Wave 52 is the first wave to exercise the SectorLogin branch, where `player->SendGalaxyMap(m_SystemName, m_SectorName, "")` (line 344) emits 0x0097 GALAXY_MAP and `player->SendClientType(m_SectorData->sector_type)` (line 347) emits 0x003C CLIENT_TYPE. Both are unconditional, no payload-shape guards.
      Architecture problem — every `StartSector[race*3+profession]` entry is a station id > 9999 (Terran Warrior=10151, JE=10521, Progen Sentinel=10301, etc., per `archive/kyp-snapshot/linux-port-legacy/StaticData.h:38-48`). On a freshly-created character, `Player::ReadSavedData` at `server/src/PlayerSaves.cpp:208-237` finds no `avatar_level_info` row → takes the `ReInitializeSavedData` path → `PlayerSaves.cpp:991-994` resets `PlayerIndex()->SetSectorNum(start_sector)` to the race/class station id BEFORE the dispatch reads `GetSectorNum()`. So a single-login attempt with `sectorId=1015` (Luna space, sector_type=ST_PLANET) gets overridden to 10151 and routes to StationLogin — the first attempt failed exactly this way. Diagnostic dump of `Session.HandshakeOpcodes` for the failing attempt: `0x00A5,0x001D,0x0034,0x007F,0x0004,0x0089,0x0040,0x001B,0x0004,0x00B4,0x0011,0x0037,0x0047,0x0061,0x0010,0x00B2,0x0089,0x003E,0x0025,0x0025,0x0025,0x0025,0x001D,0x004F,0x0052,0x0005` — 26 frames, every one matches an opcode already covered by Waves 32/34/35, and neither 0x003C nor 0x0097 appears. Server log confirmed: `Station login for player SpaceHs [42aea636]` (from `SectorManager::StationLogin` at `server/src/SectorManager.cpp:465 LogMessage`).
      Solution — NEW 2-stage login pattern. Stage 1: `EstablishAsync(sectorId=10151)` creates the avatar and runs the standard StationLogin handshake; the first-login `ReInitializeSavedData` writes the `avatar_level_info` row. Stage 2: NEW `SectorHandshake.ReestablishAsync(server, ticket, slot, sectorId=1015)` helper at `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorHandshake.cs` skips `CreateCharacterOnSlotAsync` and re-runs `GlobalConnect → DrainUntilOpcode(GlobalAvatarList) → RequestTicketAsync → DoMasterJoinAsync → DoSectorLoginUntilStartAsync` with `ToSectorID=1015`. On the second login `Player::ReadSavedData` finds the `avatar_level_info` row → takes the `ReloadSavedData` path at `PlayerSaves.cpp:271-` which preserves the sector_num set by `Player::HandleLogin` (from the LOGIN packet's `ToSectorID`) via the `secNum`-save-then-`Reset()`-then-restore at `PlayerSaves.cpp:289-291`. `g_ServerMgr->GetSectorManager(1015)` returns the SectorManager whose `m_SectorID=1015 < 9999` → `HandleSectorLogin` dispatches to `SectorLogin` (the `m_SectorID > 9999` test is false), and the two emits land in `Session.HandshakeOpcodes`. Server log confirmed: `Sector login for player SpaceHs [42aea636]` (from `SectorManager::SectorLogin` at `server/src/SectorManager.cpp:342 LogMessage`).
      G_ERROR_ACCOUNT_IN_USE — second failure on first `ReestablishAsync` attempt: stage-2 `GlobalConnect` got G_ERROR code=13 (`UDP_Global.cpp:166-170` `Attempt to log into 2 accounts? %s`) because a bare `await session.DisposeAsync()` TCP close didn't notify the server quickly enough to clear `account_in_use`. Fixed by sending an explicit `0x00B9 LOGOFF_REQUEST` (8B zero payload — handler ignores) on the stage-1 sector connection and draining `0x00BA LOGOFF_CONFIRMATION` before tearing down. `Player::HandleLogoffRequest` at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:7709-7720` runs `LeaveGroup` → `SendLogoffConfirmation` → `DropPlayerFromGalaxy` synchronously, which clears the in-memory Player so the stage-2 ticket reuse is accepted.
      Why this is a legit +2 ratchet (not a Coverage-Cheat) — both opcodes are server-originated emits that have always been produced on every space-sector handshake. No new server behaviour, no new permissiveness, no widened input acceptance, no relaxed validation. The test pattern (auth ticket → 2 separate sector logins on the same account, with explicit logoff between) is exactly what the retail Win32 client does when a player logs in at a station, then warps to space, then disconnects-and-reconnects later. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity: this is the "tightening" the rule welcomes (we now reject regression classes that vanish either emit, that swap the dispatch-branch test direction, that drop the SectorManager loading for space sectors, etc.). Adds `0x0097 GALAXY_MAP` to `OpcodeId.Known` (was missing — only 0x003C was there).
      Seam-discovery — Wave 52 introduces the FIRST 2-stage login test in the suite. Opens a family of follow-on waves: `m_ObjectMgr->SendAllNavs(player)` at SectorManager.cpp:369 (the SPACE branch's nav-fanout, which emits an array of nav opcodes only on space-sector login); `SendShipInfo` with `SpeedFactor=1` for ST_SPACE vs `SpeedFactor=2` for stations at SectorManager.cpp:360-361 (the SpeedFactor field in SHIP_INFO differs between the two paths — a passive observation on the same wire frame); `SendStarbaseSet(0, 0)` at `StationLogin2` (StationLogin-only) vs nothing on the SectorLogin2 path (passive negative-observation). - [x] Wave 51 (2026-05-27): 0x2017 RESEND_PACKET_SEQUENCE (`ReSendOpcodes`, packet_num=0xFFFF miss-path) **survival-probe** — twenty-fourth direct-stimulus wave (survival-probe; client→server one-shot with ZERO observable wire reply, connection survival verified via REQUEST_TIME→CLIENT_SET_TIME round-trip). +1 ratchet 81/207 → **82/207 (39.6%)**.
      Status: done — `SectorResendPacketSequenceTests.ResendPacketSequence_MissPacketNum_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` written; build green; test passes 1/1 in 7s.
      Pattern — client sends 6B host-LE `{short packet_num=0xFFFF; short pad=0; short opcode_count=0}` on the sector connection. Note the 2-byte gap baked into the wire shape: `ReSendOpcodes` at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:263-291` reads `long packet_num = *((short*) &data[0])` (sign-extends host-LE short at offset 0 to long; 0xFFFF → -1 on both Win32 sizeof(long)==4 and Linux x86_64 sizeof(long)==8) and `long opcode_count = *((short*) &data[4])` (reads short at offset 4, NOT offset 2 — `data[2..4]` is intentionally skipped, retail wire shape with architecture-padding the client emits matching the original 4B-aligned struct). Handler emits one `LogMessage("Opcode re-send #%x (%s)\n", ...)` line to server stdout (never on the wire). The `if (m_UDPConnection)` guard at line 272 is non-null for a logged-in sector character so the body runs. The for-loop walks `m_ResendQueue[0..RESEND_ELEMENTS)` looking for a slot with `packet_num == -1`; ctor-init in `Player::Player` sets every slot's `packet_num` to 0; loop runs to completion without taking the `break` branch. Result: zero SendOpcode, zero m_UDPConnection->SendOpcode, zero state mutation visible to the client. Even a HIT case would fire `m_UDPConnection->SendOpcode` (the UDP-direct path) which our TCP-only test client doesn't observe — so this is a pure survival probe regardless of queue state.
      Why this wave target (the long-form triage) — after Wave 50 closed 0x0028 INVENTORY_SORT, the dispatch-list survey for Wave 51 examined: **0x0082 RECUSTOMIZE_SHIP_DONE** (SaveDatabase mutation — too heavy), **0x0084 RECUSTOMIZE_AVATAR_DONE** (same), **0x008D INCAPACITANCE_REQUEST** (ABANDONED — Wave 29 commit `c13fbed` documented the first-time `m_IncapAvatarSent` branch at `PlayerConnection.cpp:11069-11104` deterministically crashes the server via shared NPC template state mutation `NPCs->Avatar.shirt_primary_color[0] += 0.1f` and emits 0x0061 AVATAR_DESCRIPTION through that crashing path; the unconditional 0x0054 TALK_TREE emit at line 11067 happens BEFORE the crash but the connection dies after — too risky for parallel-test stability), **0x0098 GALAXY_MAP_REQUEST** (emits 0x2011 GALAXY_MAP_CACHE which the proxy guard at `UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:568` blocks — opcode > 0x0FFF terminates the inner-tuple loop), **0x009B WARP** (state-mutating), **0x00BC CTA_REQUEST** (sizeof(long) stack-write bug at `PlayerConnection.cpp:7740-7741` writing 8B into 4B slots in 9B CTAResponse array — 3-byte stack smash on Linux x86_64), **0x00C5 GUILD_LEADER_ACCEPT_CLIENT** (unbounded strncpy at `PlayerGuild.cpp:746-751`), **0x3004 PLAYER_SHIP_SENT** (FinishLogin re-entry on already-logged-in player — could double-emit StartAck/SetCredits/SaveDatabase). **0x2017 RESEND_PACKET_SEQUENCE survives every concern**: pure read of m_ResendQueue, no state mutation, no SendOpcode, no SEGV class, no proxy-layer block, no FinishLogin double-fire.

Pivoted to 0x2017 RESEND_PACKET_SEQUENCE survival probe. **Workflow lesson** — before committing to ANY new opcode wave target, grep `TestedOpcodes.cs` for the proposed opcode value to find any prior-wave abandonment notes. Cite-on-cite cross-references are load-bearing for catching this class of mistake.
      Why packet_num=0xFFFF specifically — any value not in `m_ResendQueue` works for the miss-case; 0xFFFF is canonical because it sign-extends to -1 on both Win32 (sizeof(long)==4) and Linux x86_64 (sizeof(long)==8), and -1 is the standard retail wire-format "definitely not in the queue" value. The queue's slots are all `{packet_num=0, ...}` at session start so even 0xFFFE, 0x0001, 0x0002 etc. would also miss; 0xFFFF is the canonical choice.
      Seam-discovery pattern — Wave 51 introduces a NEW variant: **"client→server retransmit-request handler with zero-match queue lookup on freshly-logged-in player"**, distinct from prior survival-probe patterns because the miss-case path goes via a queue-walk that COULD have emitted (HIT case fires m_UDPConnection->SendOpcode via UDP-direct path) but doesn't on the freshly-logged-in player whose resend-queue is still ctor-init zeroed. The UDP-direct path on hit also wouldn't be observable on our TCP-only test client — so the test is a survival probe regardless of queue state. Catalogue now SEVEN concrete instances: Wave 44 post-switch tail no-op via ctor-init equality; Wave 45 ReplaceData equality short-circuit; Wave 46 outer-switch default fall-through; Wave 47 write-only-field setter with no reader; Wave 48 null-item-from-GetItem early-bail; Wave 50 server-only LogMessage default arm with no client-observable reply; Wave 51 zero-match queue walk on freshly-logged-in player (UDP-direct path on HIT not observable to TCP-only test client).

      Pattern — client sends an 8B packed `ManufactureData` payload `{int32 GameID=0 (LE); int32 Data=0 (network order)}` (same struct as Wave 44/45/46 — `common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:1062-1066`, ATTRIB_PACKED). The 100+ lines of state-mutating code at PlayerManufacturing.cpp:358-439 (AllowManufacture gate, ResetManuItems, ManuIndex Target/Components SetItemTemplateID, Cost/ManufactureCost calculation, Negotiate, CheckItemRequirements, quality calculations, SendAuxManu emit) all sit BEHIND the invalid-item early-bail and NEVER run on this code arm.
