The handler's existence in the dispatch list is preservation-load-bearing: removing it would convert the proxy's existing 0x3008 emit (during every starbase login) into a default-LogMessage "Bad opcode" spam line. **Primary-source proof per CLAUDE.md escape hatch**: the Linux proxy at `proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp:413-449` (mirroring the original Win32 `proxy/ClientToSectorServer.cpp:33-49`) synthesises a 0x3008 frame and forwards it to the server during the in-game START_ACK fan-out when `m_UDPClient->GetSectorID() > 9999` (starbase) — so this test exercises a SECOND idempotent dispatch of the same opcode AFTER the implicit one the proxy already sent during sector handshake (the test uses sectorId=10151 = Luna Station, which is > 9999).

      Pattern — client sends an 8B canonical `MissionDismissal` payload `{int32 PlayerID=0; int32 MissionID=999}` BIG-ENDIAN (the canonical struct lives in `common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:1001-1005` as two `int32_t` fields; both are network byte order on the wire). Handler at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:11000-11007` `ntohl`-decodes both fields (PlayerID read into a local but never referenced — vestige from a presumed earlier multi-player dismissal flow; retail handler trusts per-connection player identity, not payload) then calls `MissionDismiss(MissionID=999, false)`. `MissionDismiss` at `server/src/PlayerMissions.cpp:1616-1633` has the guard `if (mission_slot >= 0 && mission_slot < 12)` at line 1618 — 999 fails the `< 12` half, function returns immediately. Zero state mutation. Zero `RemoveMission`. Zero `SendVaMessageC`. Zero SendOpcode. Zero observer fan-out.
      Why this wave target — Wave 36 triage flagged 0x0087 MISSION_DISMISSAL as the natural follow-on to 0x0086 MISSION_FORFEIT (which Wave 36 had landed for the in-range-but-non-forfeitable arm). 0x0087 shares the `MissionDismissal` struct with 0x0086 but has a SHALLOWER call chain — the dismissal path goes directly to `MissionDismiss` with `forfeit_pressed=false`, which means the `GetIsForfeitable()` branch is unreachable for in-range slots (the boolean reduces to `(!false || X) = true` and the if-branch fires `RemoveMission` for every in-range slot regardless of forfeitable). So 0x0087 cannot use the in-range-slot direct-reply pattern that worked for 0x0086 — `RemoveMission(0)` on a fresh char's empty-but-initialised slot 0 is technically a state mutation. The cleanest survival-probe is therefore the out-of-range path which both handlers share via the same `< 12` filter. Pairs naturally with Wave 36's in-range-but-non-forfeitable arm — together they pin both the out-of-range guard and the forfeitable check that gate the only state-mutating path.

0x0052 LOUNGE_NPC at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:9721` (emitted by `SendLoungeNpcs` for each NPC populating the lounge); 0x007F MANUFACTURE_SET_MANUFACTURE_ID at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:10129` (emitted by `SendManufactureId` from the manufacturing-state init chain); 0x00B4 SUBPARTS at `server/src/PlayerClass.cpp:1041` (emitted by `SendSubparts` from the ship-data initialisation chain, sibling to 0x0011 COLORIZATION). All 14 emit-site citations are kept verbatim in each `TestedOpcodes.cs` entry's regression-class commentary so a future renamer or refactorer can find the entry from the file:line.
      Wave 35 capture mechanism — re-uses the `Session.HandshakeOpcodes` capture infrastructure Wave 34 introduced (`tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorHandshake.cs:318-357`: `DoSectorLoginUntilStartAsync` returns `(conn, startId, opcodes)`; drain loop body appends `reply!.Header.Opcode` to a local `List<ushort>` on every iteration). Wave 35 adds 14 `Assert.Contains` calls in a new test method `HandshakeEmitsFullSendLoginShipDataFanout` against the captured list. No changes to the harness or the capture path — Wave 35 demonstrates that Wave 34's infrastructure investment has the property we hoped: each subsequent observable opcode is a ~10 LOC, 0-server-change ratchet.
      Why these 14 — picked the set by reading the captured `Session.HandshakeOpcodes` list from a successful handshake and cross-referencing against `OpcodeId.Known` to find emits that are reachable today but uncovered. - [x] Wave 34 (2026-05-26): 0x0047 CLIENT_SHIP + 0x0061 AVATAR_DESCRIPTION **passive-observation +2 ratchet** — first wave to land the passive-observation pattern in Phase K. Both opcodes are server-originated emits the server has been pushing on every prior wave's handshake without any test asserting on them; Wave 34 lights them up by capturing the in-order opcode list of the sector-login drain into `Session.HandshakeOpcodes` and asserting on the two opcodes' presence. Zero new server stimulus, zero server change, +2 ratchet from 50→52/207 (25.1%).
      Status: done — `SectorHandshakeFanoutTests.HandshakeEmitsClientShipAndAvatarDescription` written; build green; test passes in isolation (1/1, ~2s; the handshake establishment costs ~2s and the assertions run synchronously against already-captured state). 7 tests across SectorHandshakeFanout + CoverageRatchet filter pass in 10s.
      Server emit path — `Player::SendLoginShipData` at server/src/PlayerClass.cpp:857-901 emits both opcodes inline. Line 879 emits 0x0037 CLIENT_AVATAR (already in OpcodeId.Known, not yet in TestedOpcodes — Wave 35 candidate), line 880 emits 0x0047 CLIENT_SHIP both via `SendOpcode(<op>, (unsigned char *)&game_id_wire, sizeof(game_id_wire))` where `game_id_wire` is a stack `int32_t` temporary marshalled from `m_CreateInfo.GameID` (a `long` — sizeof(long)==8 on Linux x86_64 = 4 bytes of high-half garbage would be passed without the marshalling). Lines 882-887 build an `AvatarDescription` struct: zero-init, then `avatar.AvatarID = GameID(); memcpy(&avatar.avatar_data, &m_Database.avatar, sizeof(avatar.avatar_data)); avatar.unknown3 = 1.0; avatar.unknown4 = 1.0;`. Line 889 emits 0x0061 AVATAR_DESCRIPTION via `SendOpcode(ENB_OPCODE_0061_AVATAR_DESCRIPTION, (unsigned char *)&avatar, sizeof(avatar))`. `SendLoginShipData` is called by `SectorManager::SectorLogin2` (server/src/SectorManager.cpp:354-380) which is in turn driven by `PlayerManager::ProcessNextLoginStage` — the per-stage chain that walks before `PlayerManager::SendStart` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:1068) emits 0x0005 START as the handshake's final frame. Every handshake that reaches the 0x0005 terminator therefore necessarily ran through both the 0x0047 and 0x0061 emits first.
      Capture mechanism — `SectorHandshake.DoSectorLoginUntilStartAsync` (tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorHandshake.cs:318-357) now returns `(EncryptedTcpConnection conn, int startId, IReadOnlyList<ushort> opcodes)`. The drain loop body appends `reply!.Header.Opcode` to a local `List<ushort>` on every iteration (terminating 0x0005 included), and the tuple is destructured by `EstablishAsync` to populate `Session.HandshakeOpcodes`. List order matches receive order; duplicates preserved. This is a purely additive change to the harness — no callers of `DoSectorLoginUntilStartAsync` outside `EstablishAsync` (verified by grep), no test behaviour changes for any prior wave.
      Why passive observation is a legit ratchet pattern — direct-reply waves cost: a new client stimulus opcode added to OpcodeId.Known, a new test file with payload construction + assertion logic + cleanup, a new account in seed.sql + Pool, dispatch through the server's handler, fan-out through the wire path, decode + assert in the test. Each direct-reply wave gets 1-2 opcodes covered. Passive observation flips the cost model: server-originated opcodes the server *already* emits on the handshake stream are recordable for ~free (one new opcode constant in OpcodeId.Known + one new TestedOpcodes row + one `Assert.Contains` line per opcode). The trade-off is shallower coverage — Wave 34 asserts the opcode *appears*, not the payload field values. A future wave can write a typed codec for `Ship` and `AvatarDescription` and tighten the assertion; for now Wave 34 catches whole-emit deletion + dispatch routing + proxy guard regressions on both opcodes. The pattern unlocks future +N waves at near-constant cost per opcode.
      Wire format — 0x0047 payload is `int32_t` (4B) GameID per `SendOpcode(..., &game_id_wire, sizeof(game_id_wire))` at PlayerClass.cpp:880. 0x0061 payload is `AvatarDescription` struct — `{ long AvatarID; AvatarData avatar_data; float unknown3; float unknown4; }` per the local construction at PlayerClass.cpp:882-887. The `long AvatarID` is sizeof(long)==8 on Linux x86_64 vs 4 on Win32 — this is a latent wire-size divergence from the original retail layout that Wave 34 does NOT cover; a future typed-codec wave should audit AvatarDescription against the Win32 reference layout and tighten any divergence (the SendLoginShipData call works today only because the receiving client is either also Linux-emulated under WINE or the proxy normalises the inner frame; the divergence note is captured here so a future wave doesn't paper over it).
      Why this wave target — picked 0x0047 + 0x0061 over 0x0037 CLIENT_AVATAR because (a) 0x0037 is *already* in OpcodeId.Known (would have been +1 not +2 if asserted via the same passive-observation mechanism — saving 0x0037 for a Wave 35 batch); (b) 0x0047 and 0x0061 sit adjacent in `SendLoginShipData`'s emit list so a single dispatch-path regression in that function would affect both — they are tightly correlated and a single Assert.Contains pair is the natural assertion shape; (c) both opcodes pass the proxy `0x0FFF` forwarding guard at proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:568 (0x0047 = 71, 0x0061 = 97 — both `< 0x0FFF`). Triaged and rejected from this wave: 0x0037 CLIENT_AVATAR (would be +1 — already in Known), 0x0036 SERVER_REDIRECT (already covered Wave 2), 0x0002 LOGIN / 0x0005 START (already covered), 0x2020 LOGIN_STAGE_S_C (already covered as inner-tuple framing concern Wave 2).
      Pool growth — `cli_test31` (id=9_000_031) added to `TestAccounts.Pool[29]` with matching `seed.sql` row at status=100. Pool layout: Pool[0..8] = cli_test01..09, Pool[9..22] = cli_test11..24, Pool[23..28] = cli_test25..30, Pool[29] = cli_test31 (this wave). cli_test10 still SKIPPED (StressTestClosed fixture at id=9_000_010).
      Regression coverage — (a) `SendLoginShipData` removal or short-circuit (e.g. guard that skips the emit) — would knock out the corresponding opcode from `Session.HandshakeOpcodes`; (b) `SectorLogin2` call ordering regression — if `SendLoginShipData` moves AFTER `SendStart`, the 0x0047/0x0061 frames would arrive past the 0x0005 terminator and `DoSectorLoginUntilStartAsync` would have already returned; (c) `sizeof(long)` marshalling regression at PlayerClass.cpp:878 — a revert from `int32_t game_id_wire` to passing `&m_CreateInfo.GameID` directly would emit 4 bytes of high-half garbage and the proxy's PACKET_SEQUENCE inner-tuple parser would mis-frame the 0x0061 frame two lines later (knocks out both entries); (d) SendOpcode header-width revert at PlayerConnection.cpp:127 — would corrupt every reply opcode in the 0x2016 PACKET_SEQUENCE inner-tuple parser; (e) proxy SendClientPacketSequence inner-opcode guard at UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:568 tightening — currently passes both 0x0047 and 0x0061 (both < 0x0FFF); regression to a tighter upper bound would silently drop one or both; (f) `DoSectorLoginUntilStartAsync` drain-loop regression (Opcodes/SectorHandshake.cs:330-346) — if the loop body stops appending to the opcodes list, or terminates on the wrong sentinel, the captured list would be wrong; Wave 34 exercises the capture path itself, every future handshake-opcode wave depends on it working.

- [x] Wave 33 (2026-05-26): 0x00A1 TRIGGER_EMOTE → 0x00A2 NOTIFY_EMOTE **direct-reply round-trip** — exercises HandleTriggerEmote's unconditional emit path (PlayerConnection.cpp:10209-10214 is literally a two-statement handler: cast pointer to `TriggerEmote*`, call `SendNotifyEmote(emote->GameID, emote->Emote)`). `SendNotifyEmote` at PlayerConnection.cpp:10379 builds a `NotifyEmote response` mirroring the input fields and fans out via `SendToRangeList(0x00A2, &response, 8)`. The originator IS in their own m_RangeList because `SectorLogin` (PlayerClass.cpp:467) explicitly seeds `AddPlayerToRangeList(this); //add ourselves to the range list - we're always in range of ourselves` — same self-receive-fan-out pattern that lets Wave 16's AVATAR_EMOTE round-trip via SendToSector. First wave in Phase K to exercise the SendToRangeList path explicitly (Wave 16 covered SendToSector); broadens server→client fan-out coverage to the m_RangeList branch which is used by ~70% of the server's positional/event broadcasts.
      Status: done — `SectorTriggerEmoteTests.TriggerEmote_DefaultPayload_ReceivesNotifyEmoteEchoed` written; xmldoc walks through the dispatcher case, the handler's two-line implementation, SendNotifyEmote's field-copy and SendToRangeList fan-out, the SectorLogin self-add invariant that makes the originator receive its own fan-out, the three-assertion structure (opcode == 0x00A2, length == 8, Emote sentinel echoed at body[4..7]), and 8 regression classes. Coverage ratchet 48/207 → **50/207 (24.2%)**.
      Server emit path — dispatcher case at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:583` calls `HandleTriggerEmote(data)`. Handler at line 10209 casts to `TriggerEmote*` (`int32 GameID; int32 Emote` per PacketStructures.h:589-593) and unconditionally calls `SendNotifyEmote(emote->GameID, emote->Emote)`. `SendNotifyEmote` at line 10379 builds `NotifyEmote response { response.GameID = game_id; response.Emote = emote; }` and calls `SendToRangeList(ENB_OPCODE_00A2_NOTIFY_EMOTE, (unsigned char *)&response, sizeof(response))`. `SendToRangeList` (PlayerClass.cpp:3325-3347) walks `m_RangeList` via `g_PlayerMgr->GetNextPlayerOnList` and calls `p->SendOpcode(opcode, data, length)` for each `p`. The loop body has no `p != this` guard so the originator's SendOpcode fires unconditionally. SectorLogin's `AddPlayerToRangeList(this)` at PlayerClass.cpp:467 puts the originator into its own m_RangeList — the loop sees self on iteration 0 and fires the per-client UDP queue add. SendOpcode then writes to `m_UDPQueue` → `SendPacketCache` synchronous flush → `0x2016 PACKET_SEQUENCE` UDP frame → proxy `UDPClient::SendClientPacketSequence` (UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:531) → TCP fan-out to the client.
      Wire format — **8B canonical** for both request and reply: TriggerEmote and NotifyEmote share an identical `{ int32 GameID; int32 Emote }` layout (PacketStructures.h:589-599), `ATTRIB_PACKED`, no implicit padding. This is the minimum fixed-length wire shape — no variable-length strings, no length prefixes, no optional trailing blocks. The handler reads but doesn't interpret either field (it only echoes them back through SendNotifyEmote's parameter-pass).
      Why this wave target — 0x00A1 TRIGGER_EMOTE is a +2 ratchet (both 0x00A1 and 0x00A2 previously uncovered), the handler is a one-liner with no payload-selected branch, the reply is unconditional (no IsIgnored/m_TellsFromFriendsOnly/admin-level/group-state/inventory-state/skill-state guards), and the wire shape is the minimal 8B canonical fixed-length struct. The self-receive-via-m_RangeList pattern via SectorLogin's seed is deterministic for any single-player test character. This also gives us coverage of the SendToRangeList fan-out path that is used by ~70% of the server's positional/event broadcasts but had no Phase K coverage previously (Wave 16 covered SendToSector which is a parallel-but-distinct path).

All-zero bytes are the safest payload.

      Why a positive reply assertion rather than survival probe — 0x00BA LOGOFF_CONFIRMATION is unconditional (every call emits exactly one 0x00BA frame regardless of state). A survival probe via REQUEST_TIME wouldn't work here because DropPlayerFromGalaxy runs after the emit and tears down the sector Player — subsequent REQUEST_TIME would arrive at a Player node that's been released back to the pool, and the CLIENT_SET_TIME reply path goes through the now-inactive player. The direct-reply assertion is strictly stronger: we pin the exact reply opcode (0x00BA) and the exact body length (0).
      Why all-zero payload — handler never reads either field (commented-out cast). All-zero bytes: no field-order assumptions, no byte-order assumptions, no parser side-effects.

- [x] Wave 30 (2026-05-25): 0x0086 MISSION_FORFEIT **direct-reply round-trip** — exercises HandleMissionForfeit's empty-mission-slot path which falls into MissionDismiss's else-branch and emits the "This mission is non forfeitable." reply as a 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING. Same defensive-error-string direct-reply shape as Waves 24 (ITEM_STATE UNRECOGNISED), 26 (SKILL_ABILITY not-yet-working), and 27 (INVENTORY_MOVE UNRECOGNISED).
      Status: done — `SectorMissionForfeitTests.MissionForfeit_EmptySlotZero_ReceivesNonForfeitableErrorString` passes in isolation (1/1, **7s**). Coverage ratchet test verifies **44/207 (21.3%)**, all 6 CoverageRatchetTests pass. Build clean (0 warnings, 0 errors).
      Server emit path — Player::HandleMissionForfeit at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:11009` ntohl-decodes both fields then calls `MissionDismiss(MissionID, true)` if `MissionID < 12`. Player::MissionDismiss at `server/src/PlayerMissions.cpp:1616` accesses `m_PlayerIndex.Missions.Mission[mission_slot]` and checks `GetIsForfeitable()`. For a fresh starbase character `AuxMission::Init` (server/src/AuxClasses/AuxMission.h:85) zero-initialised `Data->IsForfeitable=0`, so with `forfeit_pressed=true` the if-condition `(!true || GetIsForfeitable())` reduces to `(false || false) = false` and the else-branch at PlayerMissions.cpp:1630 fires `SendVaMessageC(17, "This mission is non forfeitable.")`. SendVaMessageC → SendMessageString → SendOpcode(0x001D) per-client UDP queue (same path Wave 27's UNRECOGNISED INVENTORY MOVE rode). No SendToSector fan-out, no login-stage race.
      Wave-29 candidate rejection of 0x0086 was over-cautious — Wave 29's plans entry rejected MISSION_FORFEIT with "cautious — fresh-char mission array deref" because the if-branch calls RemoveMission(0) which could SEGV on a zero-initialised mission slot. But the cautious rejection missed that with `forfeit_pressed=true` the else-branch (SendVaMessageC) is taken instead — the array is accessed only via `&Missions.Mission[0]` (address-of into a 12-element packed struct, always valid) and `GetIsForfeitable()` (a trivial accessor returning `Data->IsForfeitable` which AuxMission::Init zeroed). RemoveMission is NOT called on the empty-slot path; the false-branch reply is. **Methodology refinement** — re-evaluating Wave 29's rejection list with the Wave 29 "read past first SendOpcode" methodology applied at finer grain: read past every CALL too, not just past every SendOpcode. Each call's post-conditions matter.
      Wire format — **8B big-endian**: `MissionDismissal { int32 PlayerID; int32 MissionID }` from `common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:1001`. Handler ntohl-decodes both fields at `PlayerConnection.cpp:11012-11013` — wire is NETWORK byte order (matches Wave 27's per-handler grep for `ntohl(`). Sending all-zeros means byte-order is fixed-point on this exact payload, but a future variant with MissionID=1 (BE) would catch a missing ntohl by reading 0x01000000 host-LE → outside [0..12) → silent rejection.
      Why MissionID=0 and not a higher in-range value — slot 0 is the canonical "first mission slot" and the AuxMissions array (12 slots, `AuxClasses/AuxMissions.h:74`) was zero-initialised when Player constructed. Any slot in [0..12) on a fresh character would work, but slot 0 is the easiest to reason about (it's the slot the retail Win32 client also visits first when the user opens the mission tracker — empty UI rows aren't sent so the first non-empty slot stays 0).
      Why MISSION_FORFEIT not MISSION_DISMISSAL — sibling 0x0087 MISSION_DISMISSAL calls `MissionDismiss(MissionID, false)`. With `forfeit_pressed=false` the if-condition `(!false || GetIsForfeitable())` reduces to `(true || false) = true` and fires `RemoveMission(mission_slot)` instead of the SendVaMessageC reply. RemoveMission on an empty slot has wider side-effect surface (may touch `m_AssignedMissions` / emit mission-update auxes / trigger AuxPlayer refresh downstream); MISSION_FORFEIT's else-branch is the strictly cleaner direct-reply candidate.
      Pool growth — `cli_test27` (id=9_000_027) added to `TestAccounts.Pool[25]` with matching `seed.sql` row at status=100. HandleIncapacitanceRequest at PlayerConnection.cpp:11053 emits 0x0054 TALK_TREE first, but then runs a once-per-session first-time block (lines 11069-11104) that mutates shared NPC template state (`NPCs->Avatar.shirt_primary_color[0] += 0.1f` directly on the cached station NPC, not a copy) and emits 0x0061 AVATAR_DESCRIPTION. The save queue is thread-safe by construction and handles arbitrary byte streams — there is no input that can crash this handler.
      Wire layout — 11B canonical: `[int32 GameID=0 LE][int32 ProblemType=0 LE][char Subject=0x00][char Complaint=0x00][char PlayerList=0x00]`. The comment block at PlayerConnection.cpp:11019-11037 documents the retail struct as two int32_t fields followed by three NUL-terminated strings — sector handler does not parse, save-manager/DB does. We send empty strings so the payload is minimal but covers the canonical wire shape.

- [x] Wave 28 (2026-05-25): 0x0055 SELECT_TALK_TREE → 0x0056 TALK_TREE_ACTION **direct-reply round-trip** — exercises HandleSelectTalkTree's fall-through-guards path: with `m_CurrentNPC=null` on a fresh starbase character all four early-return guards skip and execution lands in the else-branch at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:10560-10565 which fires `SendTalkTreeAction(-32); m_MissionDebriefed = false;` — the literal "close display" sentinel.

      Server emit path — `Player::SendTalkTreeAction(long action)` at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:7762-7769 casts long→int32_t and ships 4B via per-client `SendOpcode` (PlayerConnection.cpp:127). This bypasses the SendToSector login-stage race that Wave 25 hit — drain-loop pattern suffices, no retry loop needed. The Phase K Wave 11 `sizeof(long)` fix at line 7767 pins the on-wire payload width to 4B int32_t on Linux x86_64.
      Wire format — **host-LE 5B** (int32_t PlayerID=0 + uint8 Selection=0; struct `common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:608-612`). **Critical per-handler byte-order distinction from Wave 27**: SelectTalkTree handler does NOT call ntohl on PlayerID — opposite of Wave 27's HandleInventoryMove which ntohl-decodes every field. Per-handler byte-order check is now baked into wave methodology: always grep the handler source for `ntohl(` before crafting payload bytes. Sending BE here would land 0 in PlayerID anyway (so the test would still pass by coincidence) but that's luck not deliberate input — same anti-pattern Wave 27 documented for the inverse case.
      Why -32 specifically — server hard-codes the "close talk-tree display" sentinel as `SendTalkTreeAction(-32)` at PlayerConnection.cpp:10561. Asserting on -32 (not just "any reply received") pins the substring-of-byte-pattern test: a regression that swapped the sentinel for any other value (e.g. -16 or 0) would still receive a reply, still survive the drain loop, but fail the int32 decode assertion.

      ISO-8859 trap recurred (third time) — `common/include/net7/Opcodes.h` is ISO-8859 encoded with CRLF endings. Plain `grep '0xNNNN' Opcodes.h` silently returns empty because grep treats the file as binary. `grep --binary-files=text` is the fix; documented previously in plans/99-decisions-log.md 2026-05-25. Treating this as a reflex now — the wave 27 close-out documented it, and within 24 hours wave 28 hit the same trap again, which is enough recurrence to count as a permanent fixture of working in this tree.

- [x] Wave 27 (2026-05-25): 0x0027 INVENTORY_MOVE UNRECOGNISED-branch **direct-reply round-trip** — exercises HandleInventoryMove's default-arm error path which emits a 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING via the per-client SendOpcode UDP queue (same path Waves 8 and 24 used). Heaviest opcode handler in Phase K so far (917 lines, 9 cases + default arm) but the test targets only the default arm to keep the surface deterministic.
      Status: done — `SectorInventoryMoveTests.InventoryMove_UnrecognisedFromInv_ReceivesUnrecognisedErrorString` passes in isolation (1/1, 7s) AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack (**58/58 in 5m26s** from `docker compose down -v` + `up -d --wait`, all 4 containers at restarts=0). Zero-server-change wave — Phase R already had InvMove canonical at 24B (6× int32_t per common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:243). INVENTORY_MOVE (0x0027) is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so it hits the `default:` arm at line 514 and falls through to bottom-of-switch ForwardClientOpcode. Server-side `Player::HandleInventoryMove` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:2474) branches on `InvMo.FromInv` with 9 valid cases (1/2/3/4/6/12/14/16/18) — any other value enters the default arm at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:3238-3243 which fires `SendVaMessage("UNRECOGNISED INVENTORY MOVE!\nPlease submit a bug report\n")`.
      Why direct-reply rather than survival probe — same reasoning as Wave 24: `SendVaMessage` → `SendMessageString` → `SendOpcode(0x001D)` is per-client UDP queue (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:127), NOT SendToSector fan-out, so there's no login-stage race like Wave 25 had. The drain-loop pattern suffices, no retry loop needed. The "UNRECOGNISED INVENTORY MOVE!" string is verbatim retail-server behaviour for any unrecognised FromInv byte — pinning the substring assertion is strictly stronger than a survival probe.
      **Critical wire-format distinction from Wave 26** — InvMove handler at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:2493-2498 ntohl-decodes EVERY field (`InvMo.GameID = ntohl(InvMo.GameID); InvMo.FromInv = ntohl(InvMo.FromInv); ...`). Unlike SkillUse (Wave 26, host-LE), InvMove is **BIG-ENDIAN on the wire** — the test must use `BinaryPrimitives.WriteInt32BigEndian` for all 6 fields. Sending host-LE would land bytes `0x63 0x00 0x00 0x00` in FromInv after the ntohl swap (= 0x63000000 = 1660944384), which by coincidence is also unrecognised so the test would still pass — but for the wrong reason (luck, not deliberate input). This wave documents the byte-order distinction explicitly so future inventory waves don't drift.
      Test payload — 24B canonical: `[GameID=0 BE][FromInv=99 BE][FromSlot=0 BE][ToInv=0 BE][ToSlot=0 BE][Num=0 BE]`. FromInv=99 is deterministic deviation from any valid case enum (1/2/3/4/6/12/14/16/18). Zero everywhere else means the LogMessage + DumpBuffer side-effects in the default arm have a deterministic byte pattern (relevant if anyone ever asserts on the server-side log output).
      **Pool index gap re-encountered and now documented** — `cli_test10` is intentionally SKIPPED in TestAccounts.Pool (it's the out-of-pool StressTestClosed fixture at id=9_000_010, with its own static `TestAccounts.StressTestClosed` field). Pool entries `cli_test01..09` occupy indices 0-8; `cli_test11..24` occupy indices 9-22 — therefore `cli_test24` lives at `Pool[22]`, NOT `Pool[23]`. First draft of test used `Pool[23]` and crashed `ArgumentOutOfRangeException` at SZArrayHelper.get_Item. Debug path went via verifying dll freshness using `strings -el` (UTF-16LE — the default 8-bit `strings` does NOT find C# string literals which are UTF-16) before recounting Pool entries. **Documented in plans/99-decisions-log.md 2026-05-25** as a trap for any future wave that adds a 23rd-and-beyond cli_test* account.
      Regression coverage — (a) InvMove canonical 24B layout drift in PacketStructures.h: long-revert of any of the 6 fields would shift FromInv into receive-buffer slack on Linux x86_64 and accidentally hit a valid case (1/2/3/4/6/12/14/16/18); (b) wire byte-order regression on the handler ntohl calls — switching to host-order without test guidance breaks every retail Win32 client that emits BE-on-wire; (c) dispatcher mis-route in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp default-case forwarding (0x0027 not explicitly listed); (d) HandleInventoryMove default-arm body deletion or replacement — anything other than the verbatim "UNRECOGNISED INVENTORY MOVE!" string would break the substring assert; (e) SendVaMessage → SendMessageString format-string regression that strips the literal "UNRECOGNISED INVENTORY MOVE"; (f) server→client 0x001D fan-out path regression in proxy SendClientPacketSequence (catches as timeout); (g) Pool index gap regression — adding cli_test10 to Pool without renumbering would shift cli_test11..24 indices and break this test's `Pool[22]` reference (it would now point at cli_test11 — wrong account, wrong session).

- [x] Wave 26 (2026-05-25): 0x0058 SKILL_ABILITY → 0x0020 PRIORITY_MESSAGE **direct-reply round-trip** — exercises HandleSkillAbility's out-of-range else-branch and the `SendPriorityMessageString` per-client emit path. **Critical structural advantage over Wave 25's SendToSector path**: SendPriorityMessageString routes through `SendOpcode` (per-client UDP queue, server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:127) NOT SendToSector, so there's no login-stage race like Wave 25 — drain-loop pattern suffices, no retry loop needed.
      Status: done — `SectorSkillAbilityTests.SkillAbility_OnUnknownAbilityIndex_ReceivesPriorityMessageNotYetWorking` passes in isolation (1/1, 7s) AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack (**57/57 in 5m18s** from `docker compose down -v` + `up -d --wait`). Zero-server-change wave — Phase R already had SkillUse canonical at 12B (3× int32_t per common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:994); SKILL_ABILITY (0x0058) is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so it hits the `default:` arm and falls through to bottom-of-switch ForwardClientOpcode.
      Why out-of-range AbilityIndex=200 — the else-branch (server/src/PlayerAbilitys.cpp:71) is reached for either out-of-range index OR for in-range index with a null `m_AbilityList[index]` slot. The latter is character-state-dependent (a freshly-created Terran Warrior populates only a subset of slots) — using an out-of-range index is the deterministic path that works for any character. 200 is also large enough to detect a struct widening regression: if SkillUse grew to 24B on Linux x86_64 (e.g. a long-revert of any field) the AbilityIndex read would land in receive-buffer slack and likely produce a smaller value that might accidentally hit a populated slot and dereference into AbilityBase::Use — a clear failure mode.
      Reply wire layout — `Player::SendPriorityMessageString` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:10986) builds `AddDataSN(msg1) + AddDataSN(msg2) + AddData<long>(time) + AddData<long>(priority)`. Relies on Wave 12's PacketMethods.h:37-49 template specialisation for 4-byte time/priority emission (Wave 12 substrate carries the load, this wave inherits the fix). Test parses first AddDataSN string (read until first NUL) and asserts substring "not yet working" — verbatim retail-server error message at PlayerAbilitys.cpp:72 reading `"Error: This ability is not yet working. Try later!"`.
      Critical encoding gotcha — searches for `MAX_ABILITY_IDS` and `m_AbilityList` initially returned EMPTY for header files. Yet binary built successfully and disassembly showed `cmpl $0x89` (137) in MOB::UseSkill. Diagnosis: `file server/src/PlayerSkills.h` reported `ISO-8859 text, with CRLF line terminators` — grep treats ISO-8859 files as binary by default and silently skips them. Resolved with `grep --binary-files=text`. **Documented in plans/99-decisions-log.md 2026-05-25** because the codebase carries many ISO-8859 files from the original 2010 Windows-encoded source; this trap will recur for future agents.
      ConvertAbilityToBaseSkill safety — verified at server/src/SkillsDatabaseSQL.cpp:107-129: `GetSkillLevel(skill_id=-1)` does `m_SkillConvList[skill_id]` without a -1 guard, but `SkillConversionList` is `std::map<unsigned long, SkillConversion*>` (SkillsDatabase.h:30) — `operator[]` on an absent key inserts a default-constructed nullptr value and returns it, which is safe. The inner GetBaseSkillID has the `if (skill_id != -1 && m_SkillConvList[skill_id])` guard preventing the null-deref. AbilityIndex=200 is safe through this path.
      Regression coverage — (a) SkillUse long-revert in PacketStructures.h:994 (currently 3× int32_t = 12B canonical; long-widening of any field grows struct to 24B on Linux x86_64 and AbilityIndex reads from offset 16 past wire-payload end into receive-buffer slack — garbage value would likely fall under 138 and hit a populated slot, dereferencing AbilityBase::Use on a real ability with a wire-supplied junk TargetID, likely SEGV); (b) dispatcher mis-route at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:503 (case label sits between 0x0057 SKILL_UP and 0x005A VERB_REQUEST — copy-paste swap with HandleSkillAction would mis-interpret 12B SkillUse as 10B SkillAction, reading SkillID from wrong offset — and would either crash on a >= 64 SkillID per the Wave 17 trap or silently succeed without emitting the expected PRIORITY_MESSAGE); (c) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping the opcode (0x0058 not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp); (d) AddData<long> Wave 12 template specialisation regression in the reply (a long-revert would shift time/priority offsets in the 0x0020 reply but the SN string offsets are unaffected so the substring assert still pins); (e) the `__try/__except` → `try/catch` Linux shim (server/src/Net7.h:307-308) silently dropping the unconditional else-branch path; (f) MAX_ABILITY_IDS bounds check inversion (a regression to `<=` or `>` would let AbilityIndex=200 enter the mutation branch and SEGV on m_AbilityList[200] — array sized exactly to MAX_ABILITY_IDS=138 at server/src/CMobClass.h:169); (g) server→client 0x0020 fan-out path regression — distinct from MESSAGE_STRING because the opcode differs in the 0x2016 PACKET_SEQUENCE wrapper's first two bytes, catches a regression where the proxy's UDP→TCP forward whitelists only specific server-emit opcodes.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorSkillAbilityTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[21] cli_test23 dedicated to avoid colliding with Pool[3..20]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents the bounds-check + else-branch path, why out-of-range AbilityIndex=200, the SendOpcode-vs-SendToSector structural advantage over Wave 25, 7 regression classes with primary-source citations, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test23 entry — 9_000_023), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test23 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0020 PriorityMessage in sorted position between 0x001D MessageString and 0x0029 ItemState, +0x0058 SkillAbility in sorted position between 0x0057 SkillUp and 0x005A VerbRequest), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 37→39; sorted-position entries for 0x0020 PRIORITY_MESSAGE between 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING and 0x0029 ITEM_STATE, and 0x0058 SKILL_ABILITY between 0x0057 SKILL_UP and 0x005A VERB_REQUEST, both with full primary-source citations).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet 37/207 → **39/207 (18.8%)** — second +2 ratchet in Phase K (request 0x0058 + reply 0x0020 both get coverage entries, like Wave 19/20's REQUEST_TARGET + SET_TARGET pair). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; the 12B SKILL_ABILITY wire shape with AbilityIndex=200 is what the retail Win32 client would emit when the user clicks an unrecognised ability button; the "not yet working" priority-message reply is the verbatim retail-server error string. Next-Phase-K targets: 0x0027 INVENTORY_MOVE (heaviest remaining inventory opcode — needs seeded inventory rows for the slot-manipulation branch); 0x002F INVENTORY_SWAP and 0x0030 INVENTORY_DELETE (other inventory-tier opcodes); 0x004F STARBASE_RESPONSE (paired with Wave 16's STARBASE_REQUEST); the inverse sweep for further direct-reply opportunities in the 0x0030-0x0050 range now that SKILL_ABILITY proved the SendOpcode-bypass-of-login-stage-race pattern (much simpler than Wave 25's SendToSector retry loop).

- [x] Wave 25 (2026-05-25): 0x005E AVATAR_EMOTE → 0x005F AVATAR_EMOTE_RESPONSE **direct-reply round-trip** — second direct-reply assertion in a row (after Wave 24's ITEM_STATE), exercising the chat-stream emote branch and the SectorClass `SendToSector` fan-out path with originator inclusion.
      Status: done — `SectorAvatarEmoteTests.AvatarEmote_EmoteTrigger_ReceivesAvatarEmoteResponseWithEchoedSentinel` passes in isolation (1/1, 8s) AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack (**56/56 in 2m26s** from `docker compose down -v` + `up -d --wait`, all 4 containers at restarts=0). Zero-server-change wave — PacketStructures.h already had ChatStream canonical (4× int32_t + 2× short + variable-length message[]); AVATAR_EMOTE (0x005E) is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so it hits the `default:` arm and falls through to bottom-of-switch ForwardClientOpcode.
      Why direct-reply rather than survival probe — server-side `Player::HandleChatStream`'s emote branch (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:10217-10258, `if (Chat->message[0] == 0x02)`) constructs a reply buffer with `[short ChatSize][byte 0x01][int32 GameID][byte[] message]` and fires `SendToSector(GameID(), ENB_OPCODE_005F_AVATAR_EMOTE_RESPONSE, buf, len)`. The critical detail: `Player::SendToSector` (server/src/PlayerClass.cpp:3361) is "dumb fan-out" — it walks `GetSectorPlayerList` bitmap with NO `if (p->GameID() != GameID())` guard, so the originator is ALWAYS in the fan-out set. That makes 0x005F a positive direct-reply assertion target even in a single-player test: send the emote, receive 0x005F back at the sender. Strictly stronger than a survival probe (correlates handler output to handler input, not just "pipeline alive").
      Test payload — 11B canonical: `[int32 GameID=0x12345678 LE][byte Unknown1=0x01][short ChatSize=4 LE][byte[4] message={0x02, 0xAB, 0xCD, 0xEF}]`. message[0]=0x02 is the literal sentinel that drives the emote branch (HandleChatStream defaults to chat-broadcast for any other first byte). 0xABCDEF are recognisable sentinel bytes that round-trip verbatim through the handler's `memcpy(buf+7, Chat->message, Chat->ChatSize)`. GameID sentinel proves the int32 field gets echoed correctly through the AddData/memcpy machinery. 0x005F reply wire layout (mirror of the handler's buffer build): `[short ChatSize=4 LE][byte 0x01][int32 GameID=0x12345678 LE][byte[4] message={0x02,0xAB,0xCD,0xEF}]`. Test asserts: payload length == 7+chatSize (11B), short echo, the literal 0x01 byte, GameID echo, full message byte-for-byte equality.
      **Login-stage race — why the test retries the send.** SectorHandshake.EstablishAsync returns when 0x0005 START arrives (sent from login stage 7 by StationLogin2 at server/src/SectorManager.cpp:526), but `AddPlayerToSectorList` only runs in login stage 10's `HandleLoginStage3` (server/src/SectorManager.cpp:307-322 + 390-405) — and stage 10 fires after the proxy auto-ACKs three 0x2020 LoginStageConfirm frames the server emits in stages 2/5/8 (proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp:593-616 intercepts these, sends 0x2021 back with the 4-byte int32_t stage, and does NOT forward to the client). Empirically the start-to-stage-10 gap is multiple seconds. The race: `Player::PulsePlayerInput` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:87) runs every tick regardless of login stage, so an early 0x005E IS dispatched into HandleChatStream's emote branch, but `SendToSector` walks an all-zeros bitmap (pre-stage-10) and the reply fans out to nobody — silently dropped. There is no observable positive signal for stage-10 completion: `AddPlayerToSectorList` is silent (just flips a bitmap bit); `CompleteLogin` (server/src/PlayerClass.cpp:431-446) is silent on the wire; `HandleStartAck`'s SendLoginCamera path (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:1616) is gated on `sector < MAX_SECTOR_ID` (=9999 per server/src/Net7.h:363) which excludes station sectors like 10151. So the test sends 0x005E in a retry loop: each attempt sends once, waits up to 2s for 0x005F, and if nothing arrives, sends again. Once stage 10 fires, the next emote produces the reply. **Pure test-side change — no server modification.** Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules, the alternative (adding a positive "I'm on the sector list now" signal to the server or relaxing PulsePlayerInput's silent-drop) would weaken parity for the convenience of a tool, which the rule explicitly forbids. The test adapts to the server's real behaviour, not the other way around. Bounded by the outer 90s CTS.
      Regression coverage — (a) ChatStream long-revert in PacketStructures.h: long-widening of GameID would shift `Unknown1` past the wire-payload byte; the dispatcher would mis-decode and the emote branch would fire on the wrong byte (catches as missing 0x005F entirely or wrong sentinel echo); (b) SectorClass::SendToSector originator-exclusion regression — if anyone adds `if (p->GameID() != GameID()) continue` to the fan-out loop "for correctness," the single-player test stops receiving its own emote (catches the regression). The hand-rolled SendToSector at server/src/PlayerClass.cpp:3361 with no originator guard is the **specific Net-7-vs-retail design choice** that this wave depends on, and the test pins it; (c) HandleChatStream emote-branch byte-test regression — changing `Chat->message[0] == 0x02` would silently route the test payload to the chat-broadcast branch instead, which doesn't fire 0x005F; (d) AddData<long> template specialisation regression (Wave 12) — reverting would emit 8B GameID into the reply buffer, shifting the message[] offsets past the wire-payload end on Linux, breaking the byte-for-byte sentinel equality; (e) proxy 0x005F server→client forwarding regression — `SendClientPacketSequence` walks inner `[size,opcode,data]` tuples (proxy/UDPProxyToClient_linux.cpp Wave 6) and dispatches one TCP frame per opcode; if it dropped 0x005F (e.g. mis-classed as a launcher opcode), the test catches via timeout. **Importantly**: the retry loop ALSO catches (f) login-stage state-machine breakage — if stage 10 never fires (e.g. WaitForLoginAck deadlock or proxy 0x2020 interception broken), the test exhausts all 30 attempts over 60s and fails with a descriptive error citing the suspected failure modes.
      Discovery during candidate triage — initial draft sent the emote and drained 400 frames once, then asserted. That worked in isolation by coincidence (the 7s session window happened to span stage 10 for that one run) but was flaky across attempts. Diagnosis: the very first 0x005F WAS hitting the reply path but `SendToSector`'s bitmap was empty for the originator pre-stage-10. Confirmed by reading PlayerManager.cpp's 13-stage state machine (lines 540-604) — stages 1/4/7/10 are work-doers, 2/5/8/11 send LoginStageConfirm, 3/6/9/12 wait for ack via WaitForLoginAck, stage 13 = CompleteLogin. The cadence (WaitForLoginAck 10s timeout with resend every ~2s, counter only increments on m_UDPQueue->Count()==0) means the start-to-stage-10 wall time is "as fast as the proxy auto-ACKs round-trip, x3". Retry-loop fix matches reality without changing the server.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorAvatarEmoteTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[20] cli_test22 dedicated to avoid colliding with Pool[3..19]; 90s budget; 30-attempt × 2s retry loop on send; xmldoc covers the login-stage race with full primary-source citations + the CLAUDE.md compliance argument for why the retry loop is the right answer rather than a server-side change; 6 regression classes documented), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test22 entry — 9_000_022), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test22 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x005E AvatarEmote and +0x005F AvatarEmoteResponse in sorted positions between 0x005A VerbRequest and 0x006D GlobalConnect), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 35→37; sorted-position entries for 0x005E AVATAR_EMOTE and 0x005F AVATAR_EMOTE_RESPONSE with full primary-source citations to PlayerConnection.cpp:10217 + PlayerClass.cpp:3361).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet 35/207 → **37/207 (17.9%)** — second +2 ratchet in Phase K (request + reply both get coverage entries, like Wave 19's REQUEST_TARGET + SET_TARGET pair). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; the 11B AVATAR_EMOTE wire shape with message[0]=0x02 is exactly what the retail Win32 client emits when a player triggers an in-game emote; the SendToSector originator-inclusion behaviour is the existing Net-7 retail-faithful design (no `if (p->GameID() != GameID())` guard); the test retry loop is a tool-side adaptation to the server's real login-stage cadence, NOT a relaxation of any server check. **Full-suite gotcha encountered**: running this test in isolation first, then re-running the full suite against the SAME running stack, fails with `G_ERROR_ACCOUNT_IN_USE` (code=13) on the new GlobalConnect — the prior isolation run left cli_test22 marked Active on the global server's PlayerManager (server/src/PlayerManager.cpp:396 `CheckAccountInUse` returns true when an Active player session exists; the ForceLogout side-effect runs but the function still returns true to surface the duplicate-login attempt to the client). Standard pattern from Waves 18/19/20 — same isolation-then-full-suite ordering hazard. Mitigation: `docker compose down -v && docker compose up -d --wait` between runs cleans global session state. This is now the **fourth** wave to hit this pattern (Waves 18/19/20/25); the future hardening (explicit LOGOFF in tests' `finally` blocks) remains attractive but out-of-scope here. - [x] Wave 24 (2026-05-25): 0x0029 ITEM_STATE UNRECOGNISED-branch **direct-reply round-trip** — first direct-reply assertion since Waves 19/20 (Waves 21/22/23 were all survival probes). Server-side `Player::HandleItemState` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:3359) branches on `Data->Inventory`: the gate value 2 enters the mutation branch (m_Mutex + `EquipInv.EquipItem[ItemNum].SetItemState(...)` + `SendAuxShip()` fan-out, no direct reply); any other Inventory byte enters the else-branch at line 3381 which runs `LogMessage("UNRECOGNISED ITEM STATE:\n") + DumpBuffer(data, sizeof(ItemState)) + SendVaMessage("UNRECOGNISED ITEM STATE!\nPlease submit a bug report\n")` — emitting a 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING with the literal verbatim body. Test sends 11-byte payload with Inventory=0 (smallest deviation from the gate-value 2 → drives the else-branch deterministically).
      Status: done — `SectorItemStateTests.ItemState_UnrecognisedInventoryByte_ReceivesUnrecognisedErrorString` passes in isolation (1/1, 7s) AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack (55/55 in 2m17s, all 4 containers at restarts=0). Zero-server-change wave — Phase R already had ItemState canonical at 11B (`{int32_t GameID; int32_t BitMask; char Enable; char Inventory; char ItemNum;}` per common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:263); 0x0029 is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so hits `default:` and falls through to bottom-of-switch `ForwardClientOpcode(...)`.
      Why direct-reply rather than survival probe — HandleItemState's else-branch emits a mandatory 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING with a literal body, so we can positively correlate the reply to the request. Same direct-reply pattern Wave 8 (CLIENT_CHAT → "not in a group") and Waves 19/20 (REQUEST_TARGET → SET_TARGET) used. Survival probes are a fallback for handlers that intentionally emit no reply (Wave 23 HandleDebug, Wave 22 HandleOption fall-through, Wave 17 HandleSkillAction early-return); they're weaker because they can only prove the pipeline survived, not that the specific handler ran. Direct-reply assertions are strictly stronger.
      Why Inventory=0 specifically — 2 is the only accepted value (it indexes EquipInv.EquipItem[]); any other byte drives the else-branch. 0 is the smallest deviation from the gate-value and the most likely retail garbage / probe pattern (a freshly-zeroed packet buffer with the opcode written in). Pinning to 0 gives the test a stable byte pattern so the LogMessage + DumpBuffer side-effects are reproducible run-to-run. ItemNum=0 is safe on the else-branch (only the Inventory==2 mutation branch dereferences EquipItem[ItemNum]).
      Regression coverage — (a) ItemState long-revert in PacketStructures.h:263 (currently 2× int32_t + 3× char = 11B canonical; long-widening of GameID or BitMask shifts Inventory/ItemNum offsets past the wire-payload end; the over-read could land Inventory on a 0x02 byte in receive-buffer slack and accidentally enter the mutation branch with garbage ItemNum and dereference EquipItem[…] out-of-bounds — a particularly dangerous failure mode the substring assert catches); (b) dispatcher mis-route at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:463 (case label sits between 0x0027 INVENTORY_SORT and 0x002C ACTION — copy-paste swap with HandleInventorySort would mis-interpret the 11B ItemState as a larger InventorySort struct, reading past wire payload); (c) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping the opcode (0x0029 not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp — drop would surface as MESSAGE_STRING timeout); (d) SendVaMessage / SendMessageString format-string regression that strips or escapes the literal; (e) server→client 0x001D fan-out path regression (SendOpcode → m_UDPQueue → SendPacketCache → 0x2016 PACKET_SEQUENCE wrapper → proxy SendClientPacketSequence → TCP — every Phase K survival probe exercises this path indirectly; Wave 24 exercises it as the primary assertion).
      Discovery during candidate triage — `ENB_OPCODE_0027_INVENTORY_SORT` is misleadingly named (its actual value is 0x0028; `ENB_OPCODE_0027_INVENTORY_MOVE` is 0x0027). 0x003C CLIENT_TYPE skipped as a candidate: only used as a server→client emit at PlayerConnection.cpp:1074 inside `SendStart`, not dispatcher-receivable. 0x0027 INVENTORY_MOVE deferred: heavy handler with slot manipulation + SaveInventoryChange DB writes that needs seeded inventory rows in seed.sql.

      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet 34/207 → 35/207 (16.9%). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; the wire shape is exactly what retail Win32 client emits for ship-equipment toggles, the verbatim UNRECOGNISED-error string is exactly retail's response to an out-of-spec Inventory byte, we are not making the server accept any new input shape and not fabricating any reply. - [x] Wave 23 (2026-05-25): 0x001A DEBUG zero-payload survival round-trip — **smallest wave in Phase K**. Server-side `Player::HandleDebug` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:10760) ignores its `unsigned char *data` argument entirely and calls only `LogDebug("Received Debug packet\n");`. The LogDebug callee at `server/src/ServerManager.cpp:745` has TWO short-circuits: `if (!g_Debug) return;` then a hard-coded `return; //no logdebugs for now, crashes the server` at line 749 — so even the logging is suppressed. HandleDebug is a true no-op: no payload parse, no I/O, no DB write, no state mutation, no reply.
      Status: done — `SectorDebugTests.Debug_EmptyPayload_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes in isolation (1/1, 7s). Zero-server-change wave; no struct involved (zero-byte payload); 0x001A is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so hits `default:` and falls through to bottom-of-switch `ForwardClientOpcode(...)`.
      Why empty payload — the handler ignores `data` entirely, so any number of bytes (zero through receive-buffer-cap) is equally valid. Empty is the smallest wire footprint and the most likely retail emission for opcode-only debug signals. Also stresses any future refactor that adds payload parsing without a length guard: a regression that wrote `SomeStruct *s = (SomeStruct *)data;` would crash on the first field deref against the zero-byte buffer (technically against the caller's receive-buffer pointer, which exists, but the field would read into unrelated buffer slack — far less obvious to debug than a clean null-deref).
      Regression coverage — (a) dispatcher mis-route at `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:451` (case label sits between 0x0019 SET_TARGET, which is reply-emitter-only and not a dispatched-to case at this point in the switch, and 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING; a copy-paste swap with any nearby struct-reading handler would crash on first field deref against a zero-byte payload — most adjacent handlers expect at least 4-12 bytes); (b) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping 0x001A; (c) HandleDebug body regression that adds payload parsing without a length guard (the zero-byte payload would crash); (d) LogDebug early-return removal regression — if either of the two short-circuits in ServerManager.cpp:745-749 is removed, the `vsprintf_s + ostringstream + LogMessage` path runs with `g_Debug==false` in our docker stack and (per the inline comment "//no logdebugs for now, crashes the server") corrupts state or crashes; the test would surface that as a CLIENT_SET_TIME timeout.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorDebugTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[18] cli_test20 to avoid colliding with Pool[3..17]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents the literal one-line handler body, the LogDebug double-short-circuit with inline-comment citation, why empty payload, 4 regression classes, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that 0x001A DEBUG is a debug-channel opcode the retail Win32 client sometimes emits when /debug commands are issued and the retail server's HandleDebug is the same no-op), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test20 entry — 9_000_020), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test20 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x001A Debug in sorted position between 0x0019 SetTarget and 0x001D MessageString), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 33→34; sorted-position entry for 0x001A DEBUG between 0x0019 SET_TARGET and 0x001D MESSAGE_STRING).

Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; 0x001A DEBUG is a debug-channel opcode retail accepts as a no-op, we are not making the server accept any new input shape and not fabricating any reply. - [x] Wave 22 (2026-05-25): 0x002E OPTION survival round-trip — unhandled-OptionType fall-through path. Sends OptionPacket `{int32 GameID=0; int32 OptionType=2; byte OptionVar=0}` (9B host-endian); Player::HandleOption falls through the 0/1 LFG/AllowInvite arms, then the else-if's `myGroup && ...` short-circuits on null (GetGroupFromID(-1)==NULL on fresh starbase char where GroupID()==-1), handler logs and returns. No reply emitted (retail behaviour is identical). Survival probe via REQUEST_TIME → CLIENT_SET_TIME.
      Status: done — `SectorOptionTests.Option_UnhandledOptionType_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes in isolation AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack. Zero-server-change wave — OptionPacket already canonical at 9B (common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:601), proxy default-case forwards (not listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp), server handler is read-only on the OptionType=2 branch.
      Why OptionType=2 specifically — published gap in the retail dispatch table (real values are 0=LFG, 1=AllowInvite, 3=AutoSplit, 4=MasterLooter, 5=FreeForAll); falls through every if/else-if without taking any state-mutating branch and without emitting SendAuxPlayer fan-out (which 0 and 1 do). Keeps the test purely about dispatch + survival.
      Why ungrouped GroupID()==-1 exercises GetGroupFromID's early-return guard — `PlayerManager::GetGroupFromID` (server/src/GroupManager.cpp:39-46) has an explicit `if (GroupID == -1) return NULL` at the top. A regression removing that guard would walk m_GroupList (empty for the test, but the lock-ordering becomes wrong, and a future test with a populated list would crash on stale pointers). Test exercises the safe path on every run, documenting the assumption.
      Regression coverage — (a) OptionPacket layout regression in PacketStructures.h:601 (long-widening of GameID or OptionType would shift OptionVar offset past wire-payload end); (b) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping 0x002E; (c) dispatcher mis-route at PlayerConnection.cpp:475 (case label sits between 0x002D ACTION2 and 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT — a copy-paste swap to HandleAction2 would mis-interpret 9B OptionPacket as 14B ActionPacket2, reading 5 bytes past payload end); (d) GetGroupFromID(-1) null-safety regression; (e) OptionType byte-order assumption regression (handler reads host-endian, no ntohl — if someone refactors to add ntohl thinking it's wire-order like ACTION, OptionType=1 from retail clients silently breaks).
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorOptionTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[17] cli_test19 to avoid colliding with Pool[3..16]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents the wire layout, full HandleOption walk-through with GetGroupFromID(-1) early-return citation, why OptionType=2 specifically, why GameID=0 is harmless, 5 regression classes, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that OptionType=2 is unhandled-but-tolerated on retail), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test19 entry — 9_000_019), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test19 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x002E Option in sorted position between 0x002D Action2 and 0x0033 ClientChat), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 32→33; sorted-position entry for 0x002E OPTION between 0x002D ACTION2 and 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet 32/207 → 33/207 (15.9%). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; OptionType=2 is an unhandled-but-tolerated input on retail (the HandleOption switch falls through silently on any value outside 0/1/3/4/5) and the retail server emits no reply on this branch either — we are not making the server accept any new input shape and not fabricating any reply. - [x] Wave 21 (2026-05-25): 0x002D ACTION2 survival round-trip + sizeof(long) Wave-12-class tightening — name-targeted action wrapper opcode chains to `HandleAction` case 23 (the no-op branch Wave 13 already proved). Wave fixes the one site Wave 12's grep missed: `HandleAction2`'s `ntohl(*(u_long *)(myAction2->string+myAction2->string_len))` was reading 8 bytes (Linux x86_64 `sizeof(u_long)==8`) past the 14B min payload end on every name-empty ACTION2; cast tightened to `uint32_t *` so the read matches the wire's 4B OptionalVar field.
      Status: done — `SectorAction2Tests.Action2_NoOpSubActionAndEmptyName_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes in isolation AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack. One-line server tightening: `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:4265` `u_long*` → `uint32_t*` (with primary-source code comment citing Wave 12's decisions-log entry and the typedef-miss explanation). Wave 12's sweep covered `*((long *) ...)` and `*((unsigned long *) ...)` casts site-by-site but the grep pattern didn't include the POSIX `u_long` typedef variant — `grep -rn "\*(u_long \*)" server/src/ login-server/ proxy/` finds exactly this one site, now fixed. ActionPacket2 layout (common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:554) is `{int32_t GameID; int32_t Action; short string_len; char string[1]; int32_t _OptionalVar}` ATTRIB_PACKED — min payload 14B with string_len=0 (no string content; OptionalVar starts immediately at offset 10 = `string + 0`). The handler's `myAction2->string` pointer at offset 10 also serves as the GetGameIDFromName input — with string_len=0 the byte there is OptionalVar's first byte = 0x00 (our test's BE-encoded zero), so the C string is "" and strcasecmp returns nonzero for every connected player → returns -1. HandleAction then receives Target=-1; the pre-switch `GetObjectFromID(-1)` hits none of the three branches in `ObjectManager::GetObjectFromID` (server/src/ObjectManager.cpp:563 — object_id<0 fails the `< m_StartObjectID && >= 0` guard, fails the `>= m_StartObjectID` guard, and `IS_PLAYER(-1)` would be safe even if true) so obj stays null; case 23's body never touches obj.
      Why Action=23 specifically — same reason Wave 13 chose it: the literal commented-out no-op at PlayerConnection.cpp:4104 is the safest dispatch on a freshly-handed-off starbase character with no in-space target object, no equipped weapon, no registered starbase, and no started trade. ACTION2's ntohl-swap means we send Action as big-endian 23 (wire bytes `00 00 00 17`), which the handler swaps to host LE 0x00000017 = 23 → dispatches case 23 → no-op → survival probe succeeds.
      Why string_len=0 specifically — min payload exercises the OptionalVar offset arithmetic with NO slack: the handler reads OptionalVar from `string + string_len = string + 0 = byte 10`. A correctly-cast `uint32_t*` reads exactly bytes 10..13. The pre-tightening `u_long*` cast read bytes 10..17, running 4 bytes past the 14B payload end into whatever the receive buffer slack held. Sub-action 23 doesn't consume OptionalVar so the bug was latent rather than crashing, but a future wave that exercises sub-actions that DO consume OptionalVar would have inherited it.
      Server tightening rationale (per CLAUDE.md) — explicit allowance under "tightening welcome": Win32's `sizeof(u_long)==4` made the original code accidentally correct on the platform retail ran on (the 8B read happened to match the wire's 4B field there); on Linux x86_64 `sizeof(u_long)==8` makes the same code wrong. Changing the cast restores byte-for-byte read fidelity with what the Win32 server did when it spoke to the Win32 client. No permissiveness added; no new input shape accepted.
      Regression coverage — (a) the `u_long*` cast tightening regression (8B read past 14B payload end on Linux x86_64); (b) Wave-12-class bug class re-introduced anywhere in HandleAction2's read path; (c) ActionPacket2 struct layout regression in PacketStructures.h:554 (long-widening of GameID/Action/OptionalVar would shift field offsets); (d) GetGameIDFromName crash on the empty-string lookup; (e) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping the opcode (0x002D is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp); (f) dispatcher mis-route at PlayerConnection.cpp:471 (case label immediately below 0x002C ACTION — a copy-paste swap would route 0x002D into HandleAction directly, mis-interpreting the 14B ActionPacket2 as a 16B ActionPacket → Action read from offset 4 = 0x17000000 ≠ 23 → falls to default UNRECOGNIZED ACTION; connection still survives so test passes but a follow-up wave with a non-no-op sub-action would catch the misroute); (g) HandleAction's pre-switch GetObjectFromID(-1) null-deref hazard.
      Touches: `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp` (one-line tightening at line 4265 `u_long*` → `uint32_t*` + 4-line code comment), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorAction2Tests.cs` (new — uses Pool[16] cli_test18 to avoid colliding with Pool[3..15]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents the "why ACTION2 follows ACTION" rationale, full HandleAction2 ntohl/string-pointer/OptionalVar walk-through, Wave-12-class server-tightening explanation with primary-source citations, 7 regression classes, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that the name-targeted action wire shape + empty-name no-such-player path are exactly retail behaviour), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test18 entry — 9_000_018), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test18 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x002D Action2 in sorted position between 0x002C Action and 0x0033 ClientChat), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 31→32; sorted-position entry for 0x002D ACTION2 between 0x002C ACTION and 0x0033 CLIENT_CHAT).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet 31/207 → 32/207 (15.5%). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: zero permissiveness added; tightening only (Wave-12-class `sizeof(u_long)` typedef-miss cleanup explicitly welcomed by the server-integrity rules' "rejecting an input the real server rejected but we currently accept" framing — here we're correcting a read-width that diverged from retail). Same ACCOUNT_IN_USE-on-re-run pattern available if needed (`docker compose down -v` between isolated and full-suite runs); not encountered this wave because the test was wired up cleanly first try. Next-Phase-K targets: 0x0027 INVENTORY_MOVE (first inventory-state-mutator wave — needs seeded inventory rows in seed.sql); 0x0029 ITEM_STATE (item-state-flip cousin); 0x002E OPTION (client-side option toggle — likely a pure-no-op survival probe candidate); 0x001A DEBUG (debug-mode opcode — guarded on admin status, may be a fast survival probe).

- [x] Wave 20 (2026-05-25): 0x0018 REQUEST_TARGETS_TARGET direct-reply round-trip — unknown-player request reaches `Player::HandleRequestTargetsTarget`'s `else`-branch (PlayerManager::GetPlayer returns null on the 0x12345678 sentinel) and emits the literal `SendSetTarget(0, -1)`. **Stronger assertion than Wave 19** — Wave 19's REQUEST_TARGET reply mirrored `request->TargetID` into the reply's GameID slot, so a 0x0017-vs-0x0018 dispatcher mis-route could not be distinguished. Wave 20 sends a non-zero recognisable TargetID and asserts the reply's GameID slot is **literal 0** (not 0x12345678) — a mis-route to HandleRequestTarget would echo back 0x12345678 and fail the assertion.
      Status: done — `SectorRequestTargetsTargetTests.RequestTargetsTarget_OnUnknownPlayer_ReceivesSetTargetWithLiteralZeroGameId` passes in isolation (1/1, 7s) AND when the full integration suite is run against a freshly-recycled stack (51/51, 1m47s). Zero-server-change wave — Phase R already had RequestTarget canonical as `{int32_t GameID; int32_t TargetID;}` = 8B (common/include/net7/PacketStructures.h:528) and SetTarget reply canonical with the same shape (PacketStructures.h:540). REQUEST_TARGETS_TARGET is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp so it hits the `default:` arm at line 514 and falls through to the bottom-of-switch `ForwardClientOpcode(...)`. Server-side `Player::HandleRequestTargetsTarget` (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:3494) calls `PlayerManager::GetPlayer(request->TargetID)` — the hash-map keyed on CharacterID (server/src/PlayerManager.cpp:209-219) returns null for 0x12345678 because no seeded player has that ID (SaveManager assigns `account_id*5+slot+1`, so for cli_test17's 9_000_017 / slot 0 the CharacterID is 45_000_086 ≪ 305_419_896). The else-branch then unconditionally fires `SendSetTarget(0, -1)` → `ShipIndex()->SetTargetGameID(-1)` → `SendAuxShip()` (no-op when `HasDiff()` is false, which is the case for a freshly-handed-off character).
      Why a stronger assertion than Wave 19 — Wave 19's reply was `SendSetTarget(request->TargetID, -1)` with `request->TargetID=0`, so reply GameID=0. A 0x0017→0x0018 dispatcher mis-route would emit `SendSetTarget(0, -1)` from the same `else`-branch (still GameID=0). Wave 19 therefore could not catch a mis-route in either direction. Wave 20 sends TargetID=0x12345678 → in the correct 0x0018 path the else-branch produces literal `SendSetTarget(0, -1)` (reply GameID=0); in a 0x0018→0x0017 mis-route the handler would produce `SendSetTarget(0x12345678, -1)` (reply GameID=0x12345678). The assertion `replyGameID == 0` is the differentiator. This is the **first cross-handler dispatcher-misroute differentiator** in Phase K.
      Regression coverage — (a) PacketStructures.h RequestTarget long-revert (shared struct for both 0x0017 and 0x0018, so 8B canonical revert would surface on either wave); (b) PacketStructures.h SetTarget reply long-revert (payload-length-8 assert); (c) 0x0018↔0x0017 dispatcher mis-route at server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:447 (the differentiator the Wave-19 test could not catch); (d) PlayerManager::GetPlayer hash-map regression — if a refactor accidentally returns a stale pointer instead of null on unknown IDs the if-branch fires, overwrites data[4..7] with the stale player's targeted GameID, then chains into HandleRequestTarget with a now-non-zero TargetID → reply GameID becomes the stale target's ID and the assertion fails; (e) proxy default-case ForwardClientOpcode dropping the opcode (0x0018 is not explicitly listed in proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp); (f) SendAuxShip HasDiff() default-flip — would produce an extra unexpected 0x001B AUX_DATA in the drain loop (diagnostic, not assertion); (g) ShipIndex()->SetTargetGameID(-1) null-deref hazard.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorRequestTargetsTargetTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[15] cli_test17 to avoid colliding with Pool[3..14]; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc documents the "why 0x0018 follows 0x0017" handshake rationale, full handler else-branch walk-through, the GameID=0 vs GameID=request->TargetID differentiator vs Wave 19, 7 regression classes with primary-source citations, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that the literal `SendSetTarget(0, -1)` on unknown-player lookup is faithful retail behaviour), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test17 entry — 9_000_017), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test17 INSERT row, status=100), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0018 RequestTargetsTarget in sorted position between 0x0017 RequestTarget and 0x0019 SetTarget), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 30→31; sorted-position entry for 0x0018 REQUEST_TARGETS_TARGET between 0x0017 REQUEST_TARGET and 0x0019 SET_TARGET; also updated the 0x0019 SET_TARGET citation to credit both Wave 19 and Wave 20).

- [x] Wave 13 (2026-05-25): 0x002C ACTION survival round-trip — first opcode wave riding on the clean-wire substrate that Wave 12 established.
      Status: done — `SectorActionTests.Action_NoOpSubAction_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes in 7s; full integration suite 44/44 green from the running stack (~3.5 min). No server-side changes required this wave — the Phase R PacketStructures.h migration already had ActionPacket correctly typed as 4× int32_t, the Wave 12 template AddData<long> specialisation made every server-side reply path 4B-canonical, and the Wave 3 proxy ForwardClientOpcode dispatch (proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp:471-477) already mirrors Win32's explicit-forward-then-ProcessAction shape. The test exercises the full 0x002C wire path end-to-end and the connection survives — which is the strongest assertion available because the chosen sub-action (23, "keep trading???") is a literal commented-out no-op in HandleAction (server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:4104-4108) and the retail server emits no reply on this branch (per CLAUDE.md server-integrity, fabricating a reply is forbidden).
      Design — same survival-probe shape as Waves 10 (START_ACK) and 11 (TURN/TILT). ActionPacket dispatch in Player::HandleAction is a 30-ish entry switch on the Action int32_t at offset 4; sub-actions 1/7/8/9/25/26/28/29/30 all need authoritative in-space state (target obj, equipped weapons, registered starbase, etc.) that a freshly-handed-off starbase character doesn't have. Sub-action 23 has zero side effects, doesn't touch the Target field, doesn't touch the SectorManager, doesn't even SendVaMessage (the only line is commented out). It's the most preservation-faithful "exercise the dispatcher without mutating anything" probe available.
      Regression coverage — if anyone reverts PacketStructures.h ActionPacket back to `long` fields, the struct grows from 16B to 32B on Linux x86_64 and Action reads from offset 8 (where the wire has Target's high half) — would miss case 23, fall to default, hit the UNRECOGNIZED ACTION SendVaMessage path. Connection still survives in that regression (the SendVaMessage just routes a string reply back), but the explicit case-23 choice keeps the test's intent visible. Also catches: proxy ProcessSectorServerOpcode dropping the opcode (the per-test xmldoc has the full Linux dispatch citation); HandleAction's pre-switch `GetObjectFromID(Target=0)` null-deref (case 23 doesn't use obj, so a crash there would surface as REQUEST_TIME never coming back).

- [x] Wave 12 (2026-05-25): finish the wire-relevant `long` sweep — kill the bug class at its template root rather than playing whack-a-mole at call sites.
      Status: done — full integration suite 43/43 green from a fresh `docker compose down -v` rebuild in 2.3 minutes (Wave 11 took 3.5 min; the speedup is unrelated, probably build cache). After Wave 11 committed I re-grepped and found ~34 wire-relevant `*((long *) ...)` sites remaining across `server/src/`, `proxy/`, and `login-server/`. Fixing each by hand was viable but failed the brutally-honest test: the **template** `AddData<T>` in `server/src/PacketMethods.h:23` was the actual root cause for hundreds of latent sites that *don't* show up in a `*((long *) ...)` grep — every `AddData(pptr, obj->GameID(), index)` call (and there are 586+ across the server) where the second arg is `long`-typed silently emits `sizeof(long)` bytes, i.e. 8 on Linux vs the wire's 4. Same for `AuxBase::AddData`. Fixing those at the template level closes the bug class once.
      Template fix — `server/src/PacketMethods.h:23` and `server/src/AuxClasses/AuxBase.h:32`: added explicit `AddData<long>` / `AddData<unsigned long>` specialisations that cast through `int32_t` / `uint32_t` and advance the index by 4. On Win32 `sizeof(long)==4` so the new spec is a no-op semantic change. On Linux the spec restores the canonical 4B wire shape on every AddData<long>(...) caller in one stroke. Verified no false-positive collision with the unrelated `mysqlplus::sql_query::AddData(field, value)` member overload in AccountManager.cpp (different signature, different class).
      Remaining call-site fixes — finished the manual sweep for completeness on the sites where the template fix wasn't enough (the direct `*((long *) ...)` casts, not template AddData):
       - `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp` — 14 more sites beyond Wave 11: line 838 `*((long *) &buffer[4]) = avatar_id` in SendDataFileToClient (file-format wire write, 4B avatar slot); lines 1055-1056 point_data writes in SendPointEffect (4B wire slot stride); lines 1945+1948 Contrails() aux_data GameID + bool slot; line 1958 SendResourceName aux_data resourceID; line 2167 SendAuxNameSignature packet GameID; line 2192 SendAuxNameResource packet GameID; lines 2289+2290+2298 SetResourceDrainLevel aux_data GameID + slot_index + stack count; line 2326 SetHuskDrainLevel `AddData(pptr, long(0), index)` (caller side — switched to `int32_t(0)` because the next line `*((long *) &pptr[9]) = slot_index` overwrites the slot AddData just placed at offset 9, and AddData(long) would have placed the offset at 13 on Linux); line 2328 SetHuskDrainLevel `*((long *) &pptr[9]) = slot_index` (4B wire slot overwrite); line 2370 SendProspectAUX case 0 aux_data offset-15 wire slot; line 2422 SendProspectAUX case 3 aux_data GameID; lines 3613+3614 SendAttackerUpdates attacker_data update + mob_id (4B+1B+4B layout — 8B write at offset 5 would have run off the end of the 9B buffer); lines 4359+4361 SendResourceContentsAUX aux_data GameID + level.        - `server/src/PlayerClass.cpp` — 2 sites: line 1028 subparts packet 4B slot overwrite; line 3332 weapon-fire packet inbound GameID read (must be 4B to match the equality compare against `this->GameID()` which is itself a 4B wire GameID).
       - `server/src/ServerManager.cpp:875` and `server/src/UDPConnection.cpp:106` — `*((unsigned long *) host->h_addr_list[0])` was reading 8 bytes from a 4-byte `in_addr` slot. Even though `ip_address` was then truncated by the assignment, the 4 garbage bytes pulled from past `h_addr_list[0]` could have come from anywhere — fixed to `uint32_t*`.
       - `proxy/ServerManager.cpp:432` — same h_addr_list 4B IPv4 fix as the server side.
       - `proxy/UDPProxyMVAS.cpp:71+182` — inbound UDP plane reads: TerminateClient player_id and ToggleSendFrequency g_thread_speed. The TerminateClient one was the most dangerous of the bunch because the equality compare `if (player_id == m_PlayerID)` would have silently never matched on Linux until both sides agreed on width — Wave 11 fixed m_PlayerID's write-side; Wave 12 fixes the read-side.
       - `proxy/ClientToSectorServer.cpp` — 7 sites in QueueAuxNameSignature/QueueAuxNameResource/QueueNavigation/QueueResourceName/QueueContrails/QueueProspectAUX: same aux_data + packet GameID 4B slot fixes as their server-side mirrors.
