- [x] Wave 11 (2026-05-25): 0x0012 TURN + 0x0013 TILT survival round-trip — sends TURN then TILT, then validates the pipe with a follow-up 0x0044 REQUEST_TIME / 0x0034 CLIENT_SET_TIME round-trip. Also: **wire-relevant `long` sweep across server-native code** (the "fix all longs" pass the user pushed for after seeing Wave 9 / Wave 10 hit the same `sizeof(long)` class repeatedly).
      Status: done — `SectorTurnTiltTests.TurnAndTilt_DoNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes; full integration suite green from a fresh `docker compose down -v` rebuild. Closes the gap on the two simplest movement opcodes (TURN/TILT — pure state mutators on `Moveable::m_Turn_Intensity` / `m_Tilt_Intensity`). Design pivot identical to Wave 10: a direct-reply assertion is **fundamentally unreachable** for movement opcodes because their fan-out happens later via `SendPositionalUpdate` on a sector tick, and the update is sent to OTHER observers in the visibility list — never back to the originating client. With a single-player integration test there is no other observer to receive the fan-out, so we use the same survival-probe shape as START_ACK: send TURN, send TILT, send REQUEST_TIME, assert CLIENT_SET_TIME echoes the sentinel tick. Pipe survival proves the server didn't crash on the local `PacketTurn` over-read, the proxy didn't drop the UDP plane on the per-opcode throttle, and `AbortProspecting()`/`WarpDrive()` guards didn't crash mid-check.
      Server fix 1 — `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:1793-1827` `HandleTurn` and `HandleTilt` local `PacketTurn` struct: `{ long GameID; float Intensity }` → `{ int32_t GameID; float Intensity }`. Win32 wire payload is 8B (4B GameID + 4B float); on Win32 `sizeof(long)==4` so the struct was 8B matching wire exactly. On Linux x86_64 `sizeof(long)==8` so the struct became 12B and `Intensity` read from offset 8 — past the end of the 8B wire payload, into undefined memory `data[8..]`. The garbage float would then go to `Moveable::Turn(intensity)` / `Moveable::Tilt(intensity)` and propagate through the physics tick on the next move — potentially as NaN.
      **Concurrent wire-relevant `long` sweep** (the user message: "can you just fix all longs? Like its obvious they are all 100% incorrect just switch them everywhere in the codebase to int32_t right?"). I pushed back on the literal interpretation — a global `s/long/int32_t/` is wrong because internal counters (loop indices, time deltas, queue API parameters like `CheckQueue(... long size, long *player_id)`) should stay 64-bit on Linux; silently narrowing them risks overflow bugs. Committed to the substantively-correct version: sweep every `long` that touches the wire — local packet struct definitions, `*((long *) data)` / `*((long *) &buffer[N])` reads/writes of inbound/outbound wire bytes, and ATTRIB_PACKED struct fields — leaving internal scratch alone. Sites swept this wave:
       - `server/src/SaveManager.cpp` ~14 sites: HandelInfraction (260-261), HandleNewRecipe (341), HandleManufactureAttempt (361), HandleAdvanceLevel (377), HandleChangeInventory (456-457 — item_id int32, cost uint32), HandleChangeEquipment (556), HandleChangeAmmo (615), HandleStorePosition (744), HandleAdvanceMission (771), HandleAdvanceMissionFlags (818), HandleMissionRemove (916), HandleMissionComplete (931), HandleDiscoverNav (1057), HandleExploreNav (1076), HandleSetSkillPoints (1109), HandleSetRegisteredStarbase (1122), HandleNewWarnLevel (1531), HandleChangeFieldRespawn (1741). All were `long X = *((long *) &data[N])` over-reads from 4B wire slots.
       - `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp` ~9 sites beyond the Wave 11 PacketTurn fix: SendOpcode wire writes (792, 796) — `*((long *) &buffer[4]) = GameID()` and `*((long *) &buffer[12]) = avatar_id` were writing 8B over 4B slots, corrupting the next 4B; wire read 873; line 1310 `long *pLong = (long *) &packet[2]` for AdvancedPositionalUpdate (slot stride must be 4B — confirmed by `length = 2 + 4 * index;` immediately below); 1679 size header; 3649 TradeAction GameID into a 5B buffer where long-write overflowed; 10191 chat-stream GameID (header sums to 2+1+4=7 per the inline comment).
       - `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp` GalaxyMap struct (10669-10674): `long Type; long Size; long PlayerID; char Variable[64]; long unknown;` → all `int32_t`. Struct went from 96B on Linux to 80B matching the Win32 wire shape (4+4+4+64+4=80). The trailing `unknown` write at 10706 also flipped to int32_t for symmetry.
       - `proxy/ClientToSectorServer.cpp` 4 sites: lines 50, 155, 157, 199 — all `*((long *) &m_RecvBuffer[0])` / `*((long *) &buffer[4])` over-reads on inbound wire. Line 157's SetStartID accepts a `long` parameter; the 4B wire read is widened on assignment which is fine.
       - `proxy/Connection.cpp` 5 sites in the RC4 key-exchange handshake: line 163 inbound length prefix `ntohl(*((unsigned long *) buffer))` → `(uint32_t *)`; line 257 outbound length prefix; 253/256/272 `sizeof(long)` → `sizeof(uint32_t)` arithmetic. The canonical wire spec is 4B big-endian length + WWRSA_BLOCK_SIZE-byte encrypted block (matches CLI client RsaHandshake.cs:101). Linux↔Linux worked by accident before — `ntohl` truncates and the LE zero-init of the high bytes made the 8B read+write effectively a 4B read+write.
       - `login-server/Net7SSL/Connection.cpp` 5 sites — mirror of `proxy/Connection.cpp` RC4 fixes (lines 164, 232, 235, 236, 247). Phase Q deleted the kyp-era TCP cluster but Net7SSL retains its own RC4 handshake for legacy callers; this side needed harmonisation to the same 4B canonical wire shape.
       - `login-server/Net7SSL/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp` + `proxy/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp` (each 2 sites): HandleDeleteCharacter + HandleGlobalTicketRequest `long X = ntohl(*(long *) m_RecvBuffer)` → `(uint32_t *)`. Same class of bug as the Wave 5 `PacketMethods.h::ExtractLong` fix that landed alongside the 0x0071 round-trip — just other call sites with the same pattern.
      What this sweep does NOT touch (and why): internal counters and time deltas in the same files (`for (long i = 0; i < count; i++)`, `long delta_ms = ...`) — those are scratch values that never see the wire, and `long` on Linux is 64-bit which is wider not narrower than Win32, so they're never the cause of wire-format drift. The `CheckQueue` queue API: `bool CheckQueue(unsigned char *pMessage, int *length, long size, long *player_id)` — the local `long player_id;` vars in `PulsePlayerInput` / `SendPacketCache` must stay `long` to match the queue's pointer type. Narrowing them would force the queue API change or introduce a cast-through-`int32_t*` aliasing trap.
      Touches: `server/src/SaveManager.cpp`, `server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp`, `proxy/ClientToSectorServer.cpp`, `proxy/Connection.cpp`, `proxy/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp`, `login-server/Net7SSL/Connection.cpp`, `login-server/Net7SSL/ClientToGlobalServer.cpp`, `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorTurnTiltTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[7] cli_test08 dedicated to avoid colliding with Pool[3..6] which are owned by SectorLogin/SectorChat/SectorRequestTime/SectorStartAck; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc covers why it's a survival probe rather than direct assertion, the Wave 11 regression class, AbortProspecting/WarpDrive guard hazards, and the CLAUDE.md server-integrity note that intensities 0.5 / -0.25 are within retail client stick range), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test08 entry), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test08 INSERT row; comments updated 9000007→9000008 and "all seven"→"all eight"), `tools/cli-client/src/CliClient.Core/Opcodes/OpcodeId.cs` (+0x0012 Turn, +0x0013 Tilt), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 20→22; entries for 0x0012 TURN and 0x0013 TILT).
      Notes: Phase K coverage ratchet: 20/207 → 22/207 (10.6%). Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules: the local `PacketTurn` struct fix is preservation-aligned (restores Win32 8B wire shape — the Linux 12B was the divergence from retail) and does not loosen any input check. The wider `long` sweep is also preservation-aligned: every site is restoring a Win32 4B wire width that Linux was over-reading or over-writing by 4B. - [x] Wave 10 (2026-05-25): 0x0006 START_ACK survival round-trip — sends START_ACK, then validates the pipe with a follow-up 0x0044 REQUEST_TIME / 0x0034 CLIENT_SET_TIME round-trip.
      Status: done — `SectorStartAckTests.StartAck_DoesNotBreakConnection_RequestTimeStillRoundTrips` passes in 7s. Closes the gap: pre-Wave-10 the START_ACK code path was untested — both the server's `Player::HandleStartAck` (`server/src/PlayerConnection.cpp:1603`) and the proxy's `ENB_OPCODE_0006_START_ACK` branch (`proxy/ClientToServer_linux_stubs.cpp:413-449`, which synthesises a 0x3008 STARBASE_LOGIN_COMPLETE for sector>9999 or 0x3004 PLAYER_SHIP_SENT for sector<9999) had no integration coverage. Now they do.
      Design pivot — original Wave 10 conception was START_ACK → 0x0092 CAMERA_CONTROL, which would have been a direct reply assertion. That is **fundamentally unreachable** for a freshly-created character: `HandleStartAck` only calls `SendLoginCamera()` when `sectorNum < MAX_SECTOR_ID` (`server/src/Net7.h:363` — `MAX_SECTOR_ID=9999`), but every entry in `StartSector[]` (`server/src/StaticData.h:63-74`) is a starbase >9999. Per CLAUDE.md server-integrity rules ("NEVER make the server accept inputs or behaviour the real server did not"), we cannot drop the MAX_SECTOR_ID guard or fabricate a CAMERA_CONTROL emit for the starbase branch — that's divergence from retail. So the test pivots to an indirect survival probe: send START_ACK + assume the proxy fires its 0x3008 follow-up, then send REQUEST_TIME and assert the echoed sentinel comes back. Pipe survival proves both opcodes processed without crashing the server or the proxy and without tearing the UDP plane during the proxy's `SetLoginComplete(true)` triple-flip.
      Touches: `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Opcodes/SectorStartAckTests.cs` (new — uses Pool[6] cli_test07 dedicated to avoid colliding with SectorLogin/SectorChat/SectorRequestTime on IsUsernameUnique; 90s budget; 400-frame drain cap; xmldoc records why CAMERA_CONTROL was the wrong target and what the survival probe actually catches), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/TestAccounts.cs` (Pool gains cli_test07 entry), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Fixtures/seed.sql` (cli_test07 INSERT row; comments updated 9000006→9000007 and "all six"→"all seven"), `tests/integration/CliClient.IntegrationTests/Coverage/TestedOpcodes.cs` (MinTestedCount 19→20; entry for 0x0006 START_ACK).
      Notes: no server or proxy changes — both paths were already wire-correct from the Wave 7 sizeof(long) sweep and the existing proxy 0x3008/0x3004 synthesis (which has been there since the Phase K Linux sector-stubs port — Wave 3). Phase K coverage ratchet: 19/207 → 20/207 (9.7%). CAMERA_CONTROL (0x0092) is **not** in TestedOpcodes — re-enable it as a real reply assertion once we have a test scenario that legitimately puts a player in an in-space sector (gate traversal from starbase, or an in-space spawn path). Removed the `OpcodeId.Known.CameraControl` enum entry as well — no test or producer currently references it, and the OpcodeId.Known list is documented as the integration-tested subset. Next-Phase-K targets: 0x0012 TURN and 0x0013 TILT (simplest movement opcodes — `sizeof(long)` review on `HandleTurn`/`HandleTilt` payloads expected, plus the new movement-fan-out path across sector players), 0x002C ACTION (combat trigger).
